# Changelog

All notable changes to this project will be documented in this file.

Format follows [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/).
Versioning follows [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html).

---

## [Unreleased]

### Added

- **Safety fuzzing phase — Miri tests, Loom concurrency models, `debug_assert` hardening, cargo-fuzz targets (PR #103)** — new `ci-safety.yml` workflow runs `cargo +nightly miri test` (UB detection on `ailake-vec`/`ailake-index`), Loom interleaving models for the compaction/scanner concurrency paths, and 7 `cargo-fuzz` targets (`fuzz/`, plus `.oss-fuzz` integration). Added `SECURITY.md` and `docs/architecture/THREAT_MODEL.md` (risk register). New `FailStore` fault-injection harness and proptest round-trips (Avro manifest, JNI/C-ABI string/IPC boundaries) exercise error paths that weren't previously covered. New `tests/tests/concurrent_search_compact.rs` stress-tests concurrent search + compaction.
- **`ailake_create_table_json` C-ABI + bindings across DuckDB/Python/Spark/Trino/Flink** — new capability creates an empty AI-Lake table (schema only, no data written) via `catalog.create_table()`, parsed from a JSON request covering warehouse/namespace/table, vector column/dim/metric/precision, `format_version`, `hnsw_m`/`hnsw_ef`, `pre_normalize`, modality, partition fields, FTS columns/tokenizer, and `embedding_model`. Wired into `duckdb-ailake` (`ailake_create_table()`, 19 arities), `ailake-py` (`ailake.create_table()`), and Spark/Trino/Flink (`createTable()` wrappers). The CLI already had `ailake create` before this change; this closes the gap on the other 5 surfaces.

### Fixed

- **Review follow-up on the safety fuzzing branch — 9 findings closed, including 2 real UB bugs (PR #103 follow-ups)** — `HnswSerializer::from_bytes` (`ailake-index/src/serialize.rs`) deserialized untrusted bincode with no bounds validation on neighbor/entry-point indices, guarded only by a `debug_assert` that compiles out in release — corrupted index bytes could reach `get_unchecked_mut`. Now validates graph structure (neighbor bounds, `max_layer`, `node_levels` consistency) and returns `Err` on corrupt input instead of trusting it. `compute_centroid_and_radius` (`ailake-vec/src/distance.rs`) now excludes non-finite embeddings before computing the centroid/radius, and NaN/Infinity embeddings are rejected at write time (`ailake-query/src/writer.rs`) instead of silently corrupting the geometric-pruning stats. Also fixed: non-finite `radius` silently lost on manifest round-trip (`serde_json` encodes NaN/Infinity as `null`), and two pre-existing Miri bugs surfaced by the branch's first real CI run (`ailake-index/src/hnsw.rs`: missing `SeedableRng` import in a Miri-only test module, and `HnswBuilder::build()` touching `rayon::current_num_threads()` before a cheap length check, triggering Stacked-Borrows UB in rayon's lazy thread-pool init under Miri).
- **`top_k`/NaN validation gaps closed across every plugin (Python, CLI, Go, C++, Spark, Trino, DuckDB)** — the `MAX_TOP_K` (100,000) and embedding-finiteness checks introduced above only lived at the `ailake-jni` C-ABI boundary; every caller reaching `ailake_query::scanner` directly (Python bindings, the CLI, and transitively Go/C++/Airflow/Airbyte via CLI shell-out) remained exposed to the same unbounded-allocation crash. New `ailake_core::MAX_TOP_K` is now the single source of truth, checked directly in `scanner::search()`/`search_multimodal()`/`search_text()`. Separately, Spark's `commit()` and Trino's `finish()` silently treated a write rejection (e.g. the new NaN/Infinity check) as a successful, snapshot-less write; DuckDB's `ailake_search`/`scan`/`write_batch`/`write_batch_multi`/`evolve_schema`/`compact` folded a real backend error into an empty/no-op result. Fixed so `ok:false` now surfaces as a real thrown error/exception in all three.

## [0.1.6] — 2026-07-14

### Fixed

- **fix(ci): set CFLAGS for ring's aarch64 cross-compile in release workflow** — cross-compilation fix for ARM64 Linux builds in the GitHub release workflow (commit `0e8eb1d`).

## [0.1.5] — 2026-07-14

### Fixed

- **`ailake-go`/`ailake-cpp` — absolute `file://` manifest-list URI double-prefixed, breaking `Search`/`search` on every locally-written table** — found building a real polyglot-read demo (`ailake-langchain-demo`'s Go/C++ clients) against a table written by `ailake-py`: `LoadTable`/`load_table()` (reads only `metadata.json`) worked, but `Search`/`search()` (needs the manifest list) failed with a corrupted path like `<warehouse>/file:/<warehouse>/.../snap-*.avro`. Root cause: `ailake-py/src/lib.rs`'s `local_catalog_store` always writes `warehouse_uri` as `file://<absolute path>` (required for Trino's Iceberg connector), so `metadata.json`'s `manifest-list` is a valid, spec-compliant absolute `file://` URI when written by the Python SDK — but neither SDK's path-join logic checked for a URI scheme, only a leading `/` (POSIX-absolute) or drive letter (Windows), so the URI was treated as relative and joined onto the warehouse root a second time. Fixed in both:
  - **`ailake-go`**: 4 call sites had the same bug independently (`resolveAvroPath` in `catalog.go`, `searchFile` in `ailake.go`, `searchFileCol` in `multimodal.go`, and `isAbsPath`/`joinPath` in `scan.go`'s `FetchRows`) — consolidated into one new `resolveWarehousePath(warehouse, path string) string` (`catalog.go`), used by all 4; `isAbsPath`/`joinPath` removed as dead code. Real gotcha found implementing this: Go's `filepath.Join`, unlike Rust's `Path::join` or Python's `os.path.join`, does **not** ignore the base when the second argument is already absolute — it normalizes both parts together, so stripping the `file://` prefix and still calling `filepath.Join` would still produce a corrupted path; the fix detects the scheme and returns the stripped path directly, bypassing `Join` entirely.
  - **`ailake-cpp`**: same root cause in `include/ailake/catalog.hpp`'s `HadoopCatalog::list_files()` (2 checks) and `resolve_path()` (1 check, not on the `search()` path but fixed for API consistency) — consolidated into one new private `resolve_warehouse_path()` method.
  - Verified against the real, live-reproduced bug (not just unit tests): a table written by `ailake-py` on a local filesystem path, read back via both the fixed `ailake-go` client (`go build` + real search, previously failed with the exact corrupted-path error, now returns real results) and the fixed `ailake-cpp` client (same table, same before/after). New regression tests: `ailake-go/scan_test.go`'s `TestResolveWarehousePath` (replaces the now-dead `TestIsAbsPath`/`TestJoinPath`) and `ailake-cpp/tests/test_catalog_paths.cpp` (new, registered in `CMakeLists.txt`'s test `foreach`), both covering the relative/OS-absolute/absolute-`file://`-URI cases. Full `go test ./...` (81 tests) and `ctest` (6 tests) green.
- **`ailake-cpp/README.md` documents `ailake::ailake`/`ailake::ailake_catalog` (namespaced CMake targets) that don't exist** — `ailake-cpp/CMakeLists.txt` defines `add_library(ailake INTERFACE)`/`add_library(ailake_catalog STATIC ...)` with no `ALIAS` anywhere; the `install(EXPORT ... NAMESPACE ailake::)` block only namespaces the installed/`find_package` consumption path, not `FetchContent`/`add_subdirectory` (the README's own primary documented example), so `target_link_libraries(my_app PRIVATE ailake::ailake ailake::ailake_catalog)` genuinely failed with "target not found" as written — confirmed building against the file, not assumed from the docs. Fixed by adding `add_library(ailake::ailake ALIAS ailake)` / `add_library(ailake::ailake_catalog ALIAS ailake_catalog)` to `CMakeLists.txt` (2 lines) rather than rewriting the README, matching the `ailake::` namespace convention the file already commits to for the installed path. Verified: a fresh `FetchContent` build using the exact namespaced target names from the README now configures and links successfully.

- **`ailake-py`'s `_ailake.pyi` stub missing `catalog_opts` — broke `compat-ailake-py` CI (`mypy` `call-arg`)** — the REST Catalog wiring below (Fase 17) added a `catalog_opts` kwarg to 14 PyO3 functions and `TableWriter.new`, but the hand-maintained `_ailake.pyi` stub — the authoritative type source for `mypy`/IDEs, since PyO3 doesn't generate stubs — was never updated to match, so every call site in `__init__.py` passing `catalog_opts` failed `mypy`'s `call-arg` check (`Too many arguments for "search"`, `Unexpected keyword argument "catalog_opts" for "TableWriter"`). Added the parameter, in the same position and with the same default (`Optional[dict[str, str]] = None`) as the real Rust signature, to all 14 stub declarations. Verified by running CI's exact command locally (`mypy ailake-py/python/ailake/ --ignore-missing-imports --no-strict-optional`) — clean, exit 0.

### Added

- **REST Catalog wiring — CLI, Python, JNI (CLAUDE.md Fase 17)** — `ailake_catalog::RestCatalog` (covers Apache Polaris, Unity Catalog, BigLake, S3 Tables, Nessie, Gravitino) existed before this change but was completely unreachable: the CLI's `--catalog` enum only listed `hadoop`/`ducklake`, zero usage existed in `ailake-py`/`ailake-jni`, and its 9 existing tests only covered synchronous URL-building — none exercised real HTTP. Added `--catalog rest` + `--rest-uri/-prefix/-warehouse/-auth/-token/-oauth-*` CLI flags (all with `AILAKE_REST_*` env fallbacks) behind the opt-in `catalog-rest` feature (matches `catalog-ducklake`'s pattern — keeps `reqwest` out of default builds); a `catalog_opts: dict[str,str]` kwarg threaded through 14 `ailake-py` PyO3 functions plus the `Table`/`SearchQuery`/`open_table` fluent layer (`local_catalog_store` is now the single fallible resolver every call site shares); and a shared `CatalogOpts`/`resolve_catalog()` flattened into the JSON request body of all 10 `ailake_*_json` C-ABI functions that build a catalog from JSON (the raw-pointer legacy `ailake_vector_search_json`/`do_search` path stays Hadoop-only — no JSON body to carry config). All three surfaces default to unchanged Hadoop behavior when the new config is omitted. **Four real, confirmed bugs found and fixed via live testing** against a real `apache/iceberg-rest-fixture:latest` container (not mocks) — the full create→insert→commit→search round trip is closed, not just the read/create side: (1) `create_table` never registered the namespace first, which spec-compliant REST servers require unlike `HadoopCatalog`'s implicit directory-based namespaces — fixed with `RestCatalog::ensure_namespace` (409-already-exists treated as success, idempotent); (2) `commit_snapshot` sent Iceberg's on-disk "no snapshot yet" sentinel (`current-snapshot-id: -1`) as a literal integer instead of converting it to JSON `null` for the REST `AssertRefSnapshotId` requirement — `IcebergMetadata`'s plain `#[serde(default)]` deserialize had no reason to special-case it, so every first commit to a fresh table failed all 5 OCC retries with the same wrong value resent each time; (3) `AddPartitionSpec` was redundantly re-sent on every schema-patch commit even for unpartitioned tables — fixed by only emitting the update when the spec actually changed; (4) `commit_snapshot` unconditionally sent `AddSchema`+`SetCurrentSchema` on *every* write commit (the schema-patch path fires on every normal write, not just real schema evolution — see `TableWriter::commit`'s `captured_schema`), even when the schema hadn't actually changed — real Iceberg core (`TableMetadata.Builder.addSchema`) *reuses an existing schema-id* whenever the submitted schema matches one already registered, silently ignoring the client-suggested id, which made the client-predicted id wrong to reference in the following `SetCurrentSchema` (this is what produced two *different* errors from the same request shape in different runs — initially misdiagnosed as a fixture inconsistency, not a client bug). Fixed by comparing the patch against the table's current schema and skipping the whole `AddSchema`/`SetCurrentSchema` trio when nothing changed — same "skip when unchanged" principle already applied to bug 3. Documented in full in new `docs/guides/REST_CATALOG.md`. Verified with 2 real `#[ignore]`-by-default integration tests in `ailake-catalog/src/rest.rs` (`live_create_table_auto_creates_namespace`, `live_ensure_namespace_is_idempotent`) plus a full `ailake-py` create→insert→commit→search round trip run 3× consecutively against a live server after bug 4's fix, all 3 succeeding; full workspace build/test/clippy/fmt clean with and without the `catalog-rest`/`rest-catalog` features.
- **Range-GET fast path for HNSW index loading (CLAUDE.md Fase 16 follow-up)** — a self-audit of the range-GET pushdown PR above found the `store.get()` full-file fetch it left in place actually contradicted `docs/CLAUDE.md` §4's own documented mmap-loading design (footer → header AILK → HNSW blob, via incremental range-GETs) — that design had never been wired into the real `search_one_file`. New `ailake-query/src/index_loader.rs::load_primary_index`: when a query needs nothing from a file besides the primary column's index (no `column_filter`/rerank/hybrid/`score_fn`/equality-delete, `IndexStatus::Ready`, non-foreign — all knowable from the manifest/config alone, before touching any file bytes), `search_one_file` skips the whole-file GET and fetches only: a speculative 64 KiB tail window to resolve `ailake.footer_offset` via `ParquetVectorReader::kv_metadata` (`parquet`'s own metadata parser only ever reads backward from a buffer's end, so a tail slice parses correctly without the whole file — with an exact one-shot follow-up `get_range` on the rare too-small-guess miss), the 64-byte AILK header, and the HNSW/IVF-PQ blob — reusing bytes already in the tail buffer when the header/blob happen to fall inside it, instead of re-fetching. Any failure in this path (parse error, out-of-bounds offset) falls back to the existing full-file GET — never turns a query that would have succeeded into one that fails, at worst wastes one small extra `get_range`. **Real bug found and fixed during implementation**: the first version resolved the AILK offset via the 24-byte `AilakeTrailer` bootstrap (cheaper — avoids needing the full footer thrift) instead of the Parquet KV entry; broke the real `multimodal_rrf_cross_modal_different_dims` test (dimension mismatch panic) because `AilakeFileWriter::write_multi` writes one **self-referencing trailer per column section** — for a multi-column file, the trailer physically nearest EOF belongs to whichever column was written *last*, not necessarily the primary one. The `vector_column == primary_col` eligibility gate correctly filtered the *query*, but trailer-bootstrap resolved to the wrong column's offset regardless, silently loading a secondary column's index with a different dimension. Fixed by switching to the `ailake.footer_offset` KV entry instead — `write_multi` always tags column `0` (primary) with that exact key regardless of how many columns follow — the same mechanism `AilakeFileReader::ailk_offset()` already prefers. Only caught because the full 341-test suite ran before merge; no range-GET-specific test alone would have caught it — a *different* feature's test (multimodal RRF) broke first. Verified with real (non-mocked) tests: `range_get_fast_path_never_touches_tabular_data_section` proves the precise, HNSW/data-ratio-independent guarantee (minimum byte offset fetched from the file is never before the AILK section start, checked against an independently-computed ground truth); `range_get_fast_path_matches_full_file_path_results` proves exact result parity (`row_id`, `distance`) against the full-file path forced via a `column_filter` matching every row (same search semantics, disqualifies the fast path). Full workspace build/test/clippy/fmt clean (343 passed, 0 regressions). Secondary/multimodal column range-GET pushdown deliberately deferred (would need a custom `AsyncFileReader` bridging `parquet::arrow::async_reader` to `Store::get_range` — bigger surface, no measured demand yet, same "defer until real volume justifies it" pattern already used for Trino/Flink Arrow in Fase 10).
- **Real predicate pushdown + concurrent per-file search in `ailake-query`'s scanner** — `docs/CLAUDE.md` §8 claimed the query pipeline already fetched files "in parallel via Tokio" and read winning rows "with predicate pushdown"; neither was true (`search()` ran a plain sequential `for` loop, and `SearchConfig` had no column-filter concept at all — not even a post-filter). Added `ailake_core::ColumnFilter`/`FilterOp`/`FilterValue` (single-column predicate: `Eq/Ne/Lt/Lte/Gt/Gte` against `I64/F64/Str/Bool`); `ailake_parquet::ParquetVectorReader::read_all_filtered` (real two-stage pushdown — row-group skip via Parquet min/max statistics, then an exact Arrow `RowFilter` on survivors, both sharing one `compare()` so they can't disagree) and `matching_row_ids` (a row-identity-preserving variant returning original file-relative positions, required because the scanner's two real call sites index rows by an externally-computed HNSW/`flat_search` `row_id` — `read_all_filtered`'s compacted output would silently return the wrong row there). Wired as `SearchConfig::column_filter`: resolved once per file before HNSW/flat-scan dispatch, with an empty match set skipping the file's HNSW search and Parquet decode entirely (the real perf win — files without the filtered value are never scanned, not just post-filtered), and a non-empty set applied as a membership check alongside the existing deletion-vector/equality-delete row skips. Concurrency: the per-file loop body was extracted into `search_one_file()` (identical logic, zero behavior change) and dispatched via `futures::future::try_join_all` — cooperative concurrency on the current task, no `tokio::spawn`, appropriate for the dozens-of-files scale this point in the pipeline already operates at post geometric-pruning. §8 corrected to describe pushdown where it actually happens (per-file row selection, not the final winners fetch) and to note file GETs are always whole-file (`store.get`), not the incremental range-GETs §4 describes in pseudocode for the lower-level mmap path — a real, separately-tracked gap (Fase 16 roadmap item), not closed here. All 10 `SearchConfig` construction sites across the workspace (CLI, JNI, Python×3, tests×8, examples) updated; not yet exposed through any public binding surface. 9 new tests (6 `ailake-parquet` reader-level, 3 `ailake-query` scanner-level integration — including an explicit row-identity check on the indexed HNSW path); full workspace build/test/clippy/fmt clean (314 passed, 0 regressions).
- **`ailake_write_batch_ipc` — Arrow IPC write path for Spark (Fase 10, ADR-017 gap fix)** — ADR-017's original ~10ms/1k-vecs estimate for the JSON embedding payload in `ailake_write_batch_json` only measured Rust-side `serde_json` decode; measured directly (JDK 21, `Float.toString`+`mkString`+UTF-8 encode — the same construction `AilakeNative.scala` performed), the real JVM-side cost is **~150ms/batch**, 15× higher. New C-ABI `ailake_write_batch_ipc(ipc_bytes: *const u8, ipc_len: i64, opts_json: *const c_char)` (`ailake-jni/src/lib.rs`) decodes a single Arrow IPC stream `RecordBatch` (id Int64 + vector column as `List<Float32>`/`FixedSizeList<Float32>` + extra text columns) via `arrow_ipc::reader::StreamReader`, replacing the JSON `"embeddings":[[...]]` payload; `ailake_write_batch_json` is unchanged and remains the fallback. `ipc_len` is `i64` (not `usize`) to pin the FFI width exactly to JNA's `long` marshalling rather than relying on platform inference. Spark's `AilakeNative.writeBatch` (public signature unchanged, so `AilakeWriteSupport.scala` needed no changes) now builds the IPC payload via public `org.apache.arrow.vector` API (`ListVector`+`UnionListWriter`, no Spark-internal Arrow helper) instead of `mkString`; `spark-plugin/build.gradle.kts` adds `arrow-vector` `compileOnly`/`testImplementation` pinned to `12.0.1` — the exact version Spark 3.5.0 itself bundles, avoiding the version-skew risk ADR-017 flagged for Arrow Flight (point 6), at much smaller scale (arrow-vector alone). **Scope correction**: only Spark currently has Arrow on its build classpath; Trino and Flink declare no Arrow dependency today (contrary to the original roadmap item's assumption) and are deliberately deferred — noted in CLAUDE.md Fase 10 to revisit once real write volume on those two engines justifies the new dependency. Verified with 6 new real (non-mocked) round-trip tests in `ailake-jni/src/lib.rs` (build a real Arrow IPC stream, write via `ailake_write_batch_ipc`, confirm via `ailake_search_json` the rows are searchable — both wire shapes, plus dim-mismatch/missing-column/null/negative-length error cases); 29 crate tests total, `cargo clippy -D warnings` clean. Every Arrow Java API call used in the Scala code was additionally checked via `javap` against the real `arrow-vector-12.0.1` jar, and the vector-construction portion (everything but the final IPC serialization) ran successfully in a real JVM program under JDK 21 — full Scala build/test wasn't possible in this environment (no `gradle`/`scalac` available), and the final serialization step hit a known JDK21-vs-Arrow-12.0.1 `MemoryUtil` incompatibility irrelevant to the plugin's actual target runtime (Spark 3.5 supports JDK 8/11/17, not 21) — documented as an open verification gap rather than glossed over. `docs/contributing/DECISIONS.md` (ADR-017) and `CLAUDE.md` Fase 10 updated with the corrected overhead figure and scope.

- **DuckLake — equality deletes now translate to a native `DELETE` (CLAUDE.md Fase 5 gap fix)** — `delete_where`/`delete_rows` always lived only in AI-Lake's own sidecar (`main.ailake_equality_deletes`), applied by AI-Lake readers only; a plain `SELECT` against `lake.<ns>.<table>` still returned the deleted rows, asymmetric with file *retirement* (compaction/decay/backfill), which already issues a real `DELETE FROM lake.tbl WHERE filename=?`. Closed for equality deletes specifically (`delete_rows`/V3 Deletion Vectors stay sidecar-only — shared Puffin mechanism across every catalog backend, not DuckLake-specific). `EqualityDeleteFile` (`ailake-catalog/src/provider.rs`) gained a transient `inline_values: Option<(String, Vec<String>)>` field (`#[serde(default, skip_serializing)]` — never persisted to the Iceberg Avro delete manifest; `manifest_commit.rs` already rebuilds the struct field-by-field for the writer, so the field drops out on its own for every backend except DuckLake). `delete_where` (`ailake-query/src/delete.rs`) now populates it with the raw `(column_name, values)` pair it already had in hand before Avro-encoding. `DuckLakeCatalog::commit_snapshot`'s `lake`-attachment transaction phase now checks `duckdb_columns()` for each equality-delete carrying `inline_values`: if the column is already DuckLake-declared, it issues `DELETE FROM lake.tbl WHERE CAST(col AS VARCHAR) IN (...)` (cast-to-string mirrors the same string-normalized comparison `EqualityDeleteFilter` already uses in the scanner, keeping native and AI-Lake masking in agreement regardless of the column's real DuckLake type); if undeclared, it logs `tracing::warn!` and falls back to sidecar-only masking (the pre-existing, now-conditional, limitation). The sidecar is always written either way, so AI-Lake readers are unaffected by whether the native path fired. Verified with real (non-mocked) round-trip tests in `ailake-catalog/src/ducklake.rs`: declared-column case (native `SELECT count(*)` reaches 0 immediately after commit) and undeclared-column case (native rows untouched, sidecar still records the delete, no error). 58 `ailake-catalog` tests + 11 `ailake-query::delete`/`equality_delete` tests green; `cargo clippy -D warnings` clean.
- **Real Iceberg column statistics (`value_counts`/`null_value_counts`/`column_sizes`/`lower_bounds`/`upper_bounds`) — CLAUDE.md Fase 5 gap fix** — these 5 manifest fields were always emitted as `null`, despite Parquet's own footer already carrying real min/max/null-count statistics (`EnabledStatistics::Page` default). New `ailake-catalog/src/column_stats.rs`: `extract_column_stats()` reads a just-written file's own Parquet footer, aggregates per-column stats across row groups (excluding the vector column(s) — no pruning value, real risk of manifest bloat), truncates string/binary bounds to 16 bytes with the standard increment-last-byte trick for upper bounds, and reuses Parquet's own little-endian numeric encoding as-is for `Int32`/`Int64`/`Float`/`Double`/`Boolean`/`ByteArray`/`FixedLenByteArray` (identical to Iceberg's Appendix D single-value serialization for every physical type `ArrowWriter` emits — no re-encoding needed). Wired into all 9 real write/merge sites (6 in `writer.rs`, 3 in `compaction.rs`); `write_manifest_file` decodes the result into the native Avro `array<record{key,value}>` shape the schema already declared for `map<int,V>`. `nan_value_counts` stays `null` (Parquet doesn't track NaN counts; low ROI for the extra scan). Enables real row-group pruning for Spark/Trino/DuckDB reading AI-Lake tables as plain Iceberg. The original roadmap item framed this as V3-exclusive/required — verified against `format/spec.md` directly that these fields are optional at v1/v2/v3 alike; not fixed sooner because nobody had populated them, not because of a version gate. Verified with a real (non-mocked) test using `apache_avro::Reader`'s own schema-driven decoder against the hand-written binary, proving exact conformance to `MANIFEST_ENTRY_SCHEMA_STR`.
- **`batch_id` idempotency survives compaction (CLAUDE.md Fase 5 gap fix)** — the merged file produced by compaction (`compact`/`compact_incremental`/`compact_deferred`) always carried `batch_id: None`, so `write_batch_idempotent`'s exact-equality check could never match it — a retry dispatched after the original file had been compacted away silently re-inserted the row. Fixed with `DataFileEntry::batch_ids()`/`merge_batch_ids()` (`ailake-catalog/src/provider.rs`): `batch_id` stays `Option<String>`, but a merged file's value is now a JSON array of every source's key (decoded before re-aggregating, so compacting an already-compacted file flattens instead of nesting). All three compaction entry-points now call `merge_batch_ids`; `write_batch_idempotent` checks membership via `batch_ids()` instead of exact string equality. Verified with real (non-mocked) tests: `merge_batch_ids`/`batch_ids` unit coverage including the merge-of-merge no-nesting case, a real `compact()` round-trip aggregating batch_ids from 3 physical files, and an end-to-end `ailake-query/src/writer.rs` regression that writes 2 idempotent batches, compacts them, and confirms retrying the original `batch_id` does not re-insert.
- **`ailake serve` — auto-compact on foreign-file detection (ADR-018 gap fix)** — `CompactionPlanner`/`CompactionExecutor` already prioritize repairing files a generic Iceberg engine rewrote (Spark/Trino `OPTIMIZE`, DuckDB — files with no AI-Lake index/`centroid_b64`, see `DataFileEntry::is_foreign`), but only when `ailake compact` is actually invoked. A long-running `ailake serve` process had no such trigger — the same foreign file degraded every `/search` call to an O(N) flat scan indefinitely until an operator ran compaction by hand. `handle_search` now calls `maybe_probe_auto_compact` after every search: rate-limited to at most one extra `list_files` catalog call per 60s (server-wide, CAS'd timestamp — not per-request), it checks for foreign files and, if any are found, fires one background `CompactionExecutor::run()` pass (`auto_compact_inflight` prevents overlapping passes). Fire-and-forget — adds no latency to the search response. `/compact` is unchanged and still available for manual/scheduled use. Verified with real (non-mocked) round-trip tests in `ailake-cli/src/serve.rs` (`HadoopCatalog` + `TableWriter` over a local filesystem store, simulating the exact manifest state left behind by an external rewrite). See ADR-018 in `docs/contributing/DECISIONS.md`.
- **`TableWriter`/`Table`/`open_table()` — `precision=` parameter for the primary (single-column) vector column** — CLI (`ailake insert --precision`) and `VectorColSpec` (multi-column writes) already exposed `"f16"`/`"f32"`/`"i8"` storage precision; the primary Python `TableWriter` constructor silently ignored it and always wrote F16, with no way to override from `ailake-py` short of routing a single column through `write_batch_multi`. Added `precision: str = "f16"` through `TableWriter.__init__` → `VectorStoragePolicy.precision`, plus the `Table`/`open_table()` fluent wrappers. Verified with a real write+search round-trip across all three precisions (file-size deltas and correct nearest-neighbour recall for each).
- **`tests/docker/demo/dags/dag_ailake_hook_ops.py`** — new demo DAG exercising the six `AilakeHook` methods that shell out to the `ailake` CLI binary (`estimate`, `delete_rows`, `decay_memories`, `add_vector_column`, `backfill_vector_column`, `migrate`), none of which were demonstrated anywhere in the demo stack. `Dockerfile.airflow` now builds and installs the `ailake` CLI binary (previously only `ailake-py` was installed, so `AilakeHook.run_cli()` had no binary to shell out to) plus the shared `embed_cmd.py` synthetic embedder. `12_airflow.ipynb` gained §8B–8D: register the two Airflow Connections the new DAG needs, trigger it, inspect task logs.

### Added (cont.)

- **`duckdb-ailake` extension wired into the demo image** — `Dockerfile` now builds `ailake-jni` + the C++ extension (`-DDUCKDB_VERSION=v1.5.0`, matching a newly-pinned `duckdb==1.5.0` pip install — previously unpinned, so the extension and Python client could silently drift apart) and copies both artifacts to `/usr/local/lib/`. `02_duckdb.ipynb` gained §10-14: load the extension and exercise `ailake_search`/`ailake_scan`/`ailake_search_text`/`ailake_search_multimodal`/`ailake_write_batch`/`ailake_delete_where`/`ailake_evolve_schema`/`ailake_compact` as real SQL, none of which the notebook touched before (it only ever proved DuckDB reads AI-Lake output as plain Parquet).

### Added (cont. 2)

- **ailake Spark plugin wired into the demo image** — new `jvm-builder` Docker stage (`gradle:8.7-jdk17`, decoupled from the Rust/Python builder) builds the shadowJar; runtime stage copies it to `/usr/local/lib/ailake-spark-plugin.jar`. `03_spark.ipynb`'s `SparkSession` now loads it via `spark.jars` + `-Dailake.native.lib`, gracefully degrading to Iceberg-only sections when the jar isn't present. Replaced the old §10/§11 print-only illustrations (found in the original audit: the "DELETE FROM" section never issued a real delete) with real `io.ailake.spark.AilakeNative` py4j calls — `deleteWhere`, `evolveSchema`, `search`, `scan`, `searchText`, `compact`, `writeBatch` — plus a documented, confirmed limitation for `searchMultimodal`/`writeBatchMulti`: raw py4j has no way to hand a genuinely `java.lang.Float`-boxed value across the wire (Python `float` always marshals to `java.lang.Double`, and Scala's `unboxToFloat` at the `Tuple3`/`VectorColSpec` unpacking site rejects it) — those two need real Scala/Java Spark code, not PySpark reflection, and are documented as such rather than faked. `ICEBERG_JAR` is now `os.environ`-overridable (was hardcoded to the container path), which is what made local verification of this notebook possible at all.

### Added (cont. 3)

- **ailake Trino plugin wired into the demo image, `ailake_native` catalog** — new `tests/docker/demo/Dockerfile.trino` (rust-builder + `gradle:8.7-jdk17` jvm-builder + `trinodb/trino:430` runtime, replacing the previous stock `trinodb/trino:460` image) and `trino-catalog/ailake_native.properties`. `04_trino.ipynb` gained §11-13: connect to the real plugin catalog, set session properties, run `EXPLAIN` and — once the two Jackson serialization bugs below were found and fixed — a real, executed `SELECT` against `search`/`search_full`, replacing the closing note's stale claim about a `vector_search()` SQL function that was never implemented (the real design is session properties, not a table function).

### Added (cont. 4)

- **ailake Flink connector wired into a new demo service, `14_flink.ipynb`** — new `tests/docker/demo/Dockerfile.flink` (rust-builder + `gradle:8.7-jdk17` jvm-builder + `flink:1.18.1-scala_2.12-java17` runtime, single-container standalone session cluster) and a new `flink` compose profile (`docker compose --profile flink up -d`, Web UI on :8082). The main `Dockerfile` also gained a plain Flink **client** install (`FLINK_CLIENT_HOME`, `execution.target: remote`) — PyFlink was evaluated and rejected (`apache-flink==1.18.1` pins `numpy==1.21.4` via `apache-beam`, which requires Python <3.11 and cannot install on this image's Python 3.12); query vectors/text are Flink *job parameters* (`-Dpipeline.global-job-parameters.ailake.query.vector=...`, a process-launch flag with no `SET SESSION` equivalent — setting it via SQL's structured `SET 'pipeline.global-job-parameters'=...` breaks the moment the value contains a comma, which every query vector does), so the notebook drives the bundled `sql-client.sh` via `subprocess`, not a DB-API client. New notebook covers `search`, `search.mode='full'`, FTS/hybrid search, and `INSERT` — all real, executed calls; of the three JVM plugins demoed in this session, Flink and Trino ended up fully working end-to-end; Spark got 7/9 methods working (`searchMultimodal`/`writeBatchMulti` blocked by a raw-py4j float-boxing limitation, see above).

### Added (cont. 5)

- **`docs/guides/CLI_INTEGRATION.md`** — new guide for `ailake-cli`, the one integration surface with no dedicated doc before now (every other binding — Python/Go/C++/JVM — had a guide; several of them shell out to this same CLI without it ever being documented on its own terms). Covers every subcommand (`create`, `insert`, `search`, `compact`, `info`/`estimate`, `evolve`/`add-vector-column`/`backfill-vector-column`, `delete-where`/`delete-rows`, `migrate`, `decay-memories`, `serve`) with real command output captured against a live local table — not aspirational text. Documents the one sharp edge unique to the raw CLI vs. the SDKs: `insert`'s source Parquet must carry the vector column already F16-encoded as `FixedSizeBinary(dim*2)` (the SDKs quantize this internally; hand-built source files for `insert` do not get that for free). `serve`'s full HTTP request/response shapes for all four endpoints (`/search`, `/write`, `/compact`, `/info`) are documented from a real `curl` round-trip, including the previously-undocumented behavior that command errors are always plain-text on stderr, never JSON-wrapped even under `--format json`.
- **Audited and updated all 6 existing `docs/guides/*.md` against real, current source** (`GO_INTEGRATION.md`, `CPP_INTEGRATION.md`, `JVM_INTEGRATION.md`, `PYTHON_INTEGRATION.md`, `DBT_INTEGRATION.md`, `DEMO_NOTEBOOKS.md`) — closing the gap between the last several Fase entries' worth of shipped capability and what the docs actually described. Highlights: `PYTHON_INTEGRATION.md` picked up the full Fase 15 surface (`assemble_context()`'s new return shape, full `fetch_data=True` param parity, `TimestampNs`, the `Agent` class's typed-column rewrite, native `compact()`, newly-exported `add_vector_column`/`backfill_vector_column`, `write_batch_ivf_pq*`, multi-column `extra_columns`, `VectorColSpec`'s 4 new fields, the `scan()`/`estimate()` aliases) — the single largest and most stale of the six. `JVM_INTEGRATION.md` and `DEMO_NOTEBOOKS.md` both had a stale "Trino `SELECT` doesn't work" claim, now corrected to reflect the fix two entries up. `GO_INTEGRATION.md`/`CPP_INTEGRATION.md` picked up `Compact()`/`compact()` and multi-column `WriteBatch`/`write_batch_multi`, previously undocumented despite existing in source since Fase 14. `DBT_INTEGRATION.md` was found already accurate (its macros never shell out to `ailake-cli`, so Fase 13's CLI-only flags don't apply) — audited, no changes needed.

### Fixed (cont. 3)

- **`ailake-flink` — `search.mode='full'` failed every query with `NotSerializableException: org.apache.flink.table.catalog.ResolvedSchema`** — confirmed live against a real (non-local) Flink 1.18 cluster: `AilakeScanInputFormat` held the full `ResolvedSchema` object as a field, and Flink serializes `InputFormat` instances to ship to TaskManagers even in single-container standalone mode. Fixed by extracting only the serializable bits needed (`ScanColumnSpec(name: String, typeRoot: LogicalTypeRoot)`, both actually `Serializable`) at planning time in `AilakeVectorConnectorFactory`, instead of holding the schema object itself in the shipped `InputFormat`. New regression test (`inputFormatIsActuallySerializable`, round-trips the format through `ObjectOutputStream`) — no test in this repo exercised cross-process (de)serialization before this.
- **`ailake-flink` — `search.mode='full'` silently dropped the first (lowest-distance) result row** — `search.top-k=1` returned 0 rows, `top-k=5` returned 4, reproducibly, confirmed live. Traced to a manual `position: Int` field driving `reachedEnd()`/`nextRecord()` in `AilakeScanInputFormat`, which loses the first element somewhere in Flink's `InputFormatSourceFunction` driver loop (not root-caused further — cross-checked `ailake_scan_json` directly via ctypes, always correct; the sibling `search`-mode `AilakeInputFormat`, which uses a plain `Iterator<RowData>` instead of manual indexing, never showed this bug). Fixed by switching `AilakeScanInputFormat` to the same iterator-based pattern (materialize all rows in `open()`, matching the already-correct sibling implementation) instead of continuing to debug an index-based scheme against undocumented Flink runtime iteration order.

### Fixed (cont. 2)

- **`trino-plugin` — `slf4j-api` was `compileOnly`, but Trino's per-plugin classloader does not expose it** — confirmed live against a real Trino server: catalog construction failed outright with `NoClassDefFoundError: org/slf4j/LoggerFactory` at `VectorScanMetadata.<init>`, so the connector never loaded at all. Fixed by bundling `slf4j-api` into the shadowJar (`implementation` instead of `compileOnly`), matching how JNA was already bundled.
- **`trino-plugin` — `session.getProperty("top_k", Int::class.java)` used Kotlin's primitive `int.class` instead of the boxed `java.lang.Integer` `PropertyMetadata.integerProperty` registers** — `Int::class.java` in Kotlin resolves to the primitive type, not `Int::class.javaObjectType` (boxed); every query hit `INVALID_SESSION_PROPERTY: Property ... is type java.lang.Integer, but requested type was int` even for the property's own default value. Same bug at the `hybrid_weight`/`Double::class.java` call site (not yet triggered in the demo, since it needs hybrid-search session properties set — fixed proactively). Both confirmed and fixed against a live Trino 430 server; no test in this repo exercises a live server for this plugin — and `VectorScanSplitManagerTest`'s Mockito stubs were mocking the *same wrong primitive overload*, so the existing unit tests couldn't have caught this either; fixed those too (`Int::class.javaObjectType`/`Double::class.javaObjectType` in the `on { getProperty(...) }` stubs) so they now actually exercise the code path Trino calls for real.

### Fixed (cont. 4)

- **Trino plugin `SELECT` execution — two real, distinct bugs, both confirmed fixed against a live Trino 430 server** (previously documented as "found but not fixed"; `search`, `search_full` now return real rows end-to-end):
  1. **`NullPointerException` reconstructing `VectorScanTableHandle`** ("Parameter specified as non-null is null: ... parameter tableUri") inside Trino's internal `TaskUpdateRequest` JSON codec (coordinator → worker HTTP call, exercised even in single-node mode) — the *same* handle rendered with `tableUri` correctly populated in `EXPLAIN` plan text, since `EXPLAIN` never round-trips the handle through this codec. Root cause: a bare `@JsonProperty` on a Kotlin primary-constructor `val` (e.g. `@JsonProperty("tableUri") val tableUri: String`) only reaches Jackson's *parameter* use-site, which is enough for deserialization (creator param resolution) but invisible to serialization — Trino's `ObjectMapperProvider` disables `MapperFeature.AUTO_DETECT_GETTERS`/`AUTO_DETECT_FIELDS` globally (it relies on `io.airlift.json.RecordAutoDetectModule` for genuine `java.lang.Record` types instead, and these handles are Kotlin `data class`es, not records), so Jackson had no getter to read from and every field silently serialized as absent. Fixed by adding an explicit `@get:JsonProperty(...)` alongside every `@param:JsonProperty(...)` on every field of every `ConnectorTableHandle`/`ConnectorSplit`/`ColumnHandle` data class in `VectorScanHandles.kt`, `AilakeIngestTableHandle.kt`, and the nested `PartitionFieldDef`/`VectorColSpec` data classes in `AilakeNative.kt` (any of these can be embedded as a field and round-trip through the same codec).
  2. **`IllegalAccessException: class ... AnnotatedConstructor cannot access a member of class VectorScanTransactionHandle with modifiers "private"`** — surfaced only once bug 1 was fixed (a real `SELECT` never got far enough to hit it before). `VectorScanTransactionHandle` is a Kotlin `object` (stateless singleton transaction handle), which compiles to a class with a private synthetic no-arg constructor; Trino's internal Jackson mapper has no `kotlin-module` registered (unlike `AilakeNative.kt`'s own `jacksonObjectMapper()`, used only for the plugin's *own* JSON, never for Trino's internal codec) and reflected on that private constructor directly. Fixed with a `@JsonCreator @JvmStatic fun jsonCreator(): VectorScanTransactionHandle = VectorScanTransactionHandle` factory method, sidestepping the constructor entirely.

  Neither bug was reachable by `VectorScanSplitManagerTest`'s Mockito-based unit tests (no test in this repo exercises a live server's JSON codec for this plugin) — both were found and fixed by standing up the real `Dockerfile.trino` image (rust-builder + jvm-builder + `trinodb/trino:430`) against a live table and running `SELECT * FROM search` / `SELECT * FROM search_full`, not by code review. `04_trino.ipynb` §13 and `docs/specs/JVM_PLUGINS.md` updated to drop the "known limitation" framing.

### Fixed (cont. 5)

- **`ailake delete-where` silently did nothing — deleted rows kept appearing in every `search()`, masked only by an easy-to-miss `WARN` log** — found live while capturing real command output for the new `docs/guides/CLI_INTEGRATION.md`. Root cause: `delete.rs::delete_where()` wrote `EqualityDeleteFile.path` already prefixed with `table_root` (e.g. `"docs/chunks/metadata/eq-del-123.avro"`), but `commit_snapshot`'s shared commit path (`manifest_commit.rs::build_commit()`) re-prefixes any `d.path` that doesn't already start with `/` or contain `://` with `table_root` *again* — producing a double-prefixed path (`"docs/chunks/docs/chunks/metadata/eq-del-123.avro"`) that was written into the delete manifest but never existed on disk at that path. `list_equality_deletes()` → `EqualityDeleteFilter::from_files()`'s `store.get()` 404'd on every read, which `scanner.rs` (by design, for a missing/corrupt delete file) treats as non-fatal — logs `WARN: ailake: equality delete filter build failed: ... — rows may appear` and falls back to an *empty* filter, so the "delete" had zero effect on any subsequent read. This is the same class of bug as the double-path-prefix bugs found and fixed in `ailake-go` and `ailake-cpp` during Fase 14 (`docs/guides/GO_INTEGRATION.md`/`CPP_INTEGRATION.md`'s catalog-reading fixes) — same root cause (a path already relative-to-warehouse gets re-joined against the same base), different call site, first time hit on the write side. **Zero existing test coverage caught this**: every `EqualityDeleteFilter` test constructed the filter directly from hand-written relative paths (bypassing `delete_where()`/`commit_snapshot()` entirely), and `delete_rows()` (the *different*, V3-only Deletion Vector mechanism) had its own well-tested end-to-end coverage that never touched this code path. Fixed by passing a `table_root`-relative path (`"metadata/eq-del-{snap_id}.avro"`) into `EqualityDeleteFile.path` — matching the contract `build_commit()`'s prefix logic actually expects — while still using the fully-qualified path for the `store.put()` I/O call itself. New regression test `delete_where_eq_delete_file_is_loadable_after_commit` exercises the real write → commit → `list_equality_deletes` → `EqualityDeleteFilter::from_files` → `apply()` round trip (not `EqualityDeleteFilter` in isolation) — the exact path the three isolation-only tests couldn't have caught. Verified against the real `ailake` CLI binary: `create` → `insert` → `delete-where` → `search --format json` now correctly excludes deleted rows, with no warning logged.

### Fixed (cont.)

- **Metadata-only schema evolution (`evolveSchema`/`add_column`) was invisible to `ailake_scan_json`/`fetch_data=True` full-row reads** — originally discovered verifying the Spark plugin's `evolveSchema` call for real: added a nullable column via `AilakeNative.evolveSchema`, Iceberg's `metadata.json` correctly showed the new schema, but the next `AilakeNative.scan()` (and, confirmed separately, `ailake.search(fetch_data=True)`) omitted the new column entirely instead of returning it as `null` — both call the single shared `ailake_query::scanner::fetch_rows()`, which built its output schema from `collected[0]`'s *physical* Parquet file schema rather than the table's *current* Iceberg schema. Confirmed this was AI-Lake-specific, not a general Iceberg problem: a plain `spark.read.format("iceberg").load(...)` on the identical table correctly projected the new column as `NULL` on every pre-existing row. **Now fixed**: `fetch_rows()` takes the current schema's `&[SchemaField]` (already loaded by every caller for other reasons — `ailake-py`, `ailake-jni`'s `ailake_scan_json` handler) and runs each file's batch through the same `SchemaFiller::fill()` the pointer-search path (`search()`) already used, before the per-row `take()`/`concat_batches` logic — one fix point covers every full-row-fetch consumer (ailake-py `fetch_data=True`, and `ailake_scan_json` used by DuckDB/Spark/Trino/Flink) since they all funnel through this one function. Caught a second, self-inflicted bug while fixing the first: passing the *unfiltered* schema-field list to `SchemaFiller::fill()` also included the vector column itself, which `AilakeFileReader::read_parquet()` deliberately returns out-of-band (as `vectors: Vec<Vec<f32>>`, decoded and re-appended separately a few lines later) rather than as part of the tabular batch — the filler saw it as "missing" and injected a synthetic wrong-typed column for it (`iceberg_type_to_arrow`'s `Utf8` fallback), producing a *duplicate* `embedding` field that broke pandas' arrow→pandas conversion (`Unsupported cast from fixed_size_list<...> to large_utf8`) on **every** `fetch_data=True`/`scan()` call, not just evolved-schema ones — caught immediately by verifying against real pandas conversion (not just the Rust arrow API), before it shipped. Fixed by excluding the vector column by name from the field list passed to the filler. Two new regression tests in `ailake-query/src/scanner.rs` (`fetch_rows_projects_evolved_column_as_null`, `fetch_rows_does_not_duplicate_vector_column`); verified end-to-end via the real `ailake_scan_json` C-ABI (ctypes) and a rebuilt `ailake-py` wheel (`fetch_data=True` → real pandas `DataFrame`, both with and without schema evolution).
- **`duckdb-ailake/README.md` never documented the `RTLD_GLOBAL` requirement for the Python loading path** — found while wiring the extension into the demo: `LOAD '...duckdb_extension'` fails with a misleading `undefined symbol: _ZTIN6duckdb28SimpleNamedParameterFunctionE` IO error unless `sys.setdlopenflags(os.RTLD_GLOBAL)` runs *before* `import duckdb` (Python's import machinery loads C-extension modules `RTLD_LOCAL` by default, hiding DuckDB's own symbols from anything `dlopen`'d afterwards). `duckdb-ailake/test/*.py` already did this correctly; the README's "Load in Python" section — the only reference a new user would follow — did not, and would send them into the same undefined-symbol dead end this session hit. Also fixed a stale `DUCKDB_VERSION=v1.1.3` build example (doesn't compile against current sources — the extension code requires `duckdb/main/extension/extension_loader.hpp`, added well after 1.1.3) that disagreed with the file's own CMake default (`v1.5.3`) and with CI's actually-tested version; and documented (not fixed — genuinely not yet root-caused) that the official `duckdb.org` CLI binary doesn't export the same symbol at all (confirmed via `nm -D`), so the CLI-loading path in the same README doesn't currently work even with the right flags — only the Python path does, which is what this project's tests and demo actually rely on.
- **`assemble_context()` call sites still treated its return value as a plain XML string** — the native binding was changed (Fase 15) to return `{"text": str, "chunk_count": int, "token_estimate": int}`, but four real call sites were never updated: `01_ailake_demo.ipynb` §10 (would raise `KeyError` on `context_xml[:1200]` — confirmed by actually executing the notebook), `07_multimodal.ipynb` §9 and `08_agents.ipynb` §6 (printed the raw dict instead of the XML), and the live `dag_ailake_ingest_search.py` `assemble_context` task (`len(context)` silently returned `3` instead of a character count, and `context[:400]` would raise `KeyError` — this task would have crashed on every real DAG run). All four now unpack `["text"]`.
- **`01_ailake_demo.ipynb` IVF-PQ `rerank_factor` cell indexed a `row_id` column that `fetch_data=True` search results never carry** (`fetch_data=True` returns Parquet columns + `_distance`, not `row_id` — see §4's own docstring) — `KeyError` on execution. Switched to pointer-only search (`.to_list()`), which does carry `row_id`.
- **`01_ailake_demo.ipynb` — four cells read `os.environ.get("QUERY_PATH", "/data/demo_query.json")`** instead of the notebook's own `QUERY_PATH` variable (set in §0 from `DEMO_TABLE_PATH`) — `QUERY_PATH` was never an actual environment variable, so these cells silently ignored it and always read the hardcoded fallback path. Harmless under the default `DEMO_TABLE_PATH=/data/ailake_demo` (its parent happens to be `/data`) but breaks for any other table path. Fixed to reference the `QUERY_PATH` variable directly, matching every other cell in the notebook.
- **`01_ailake_demo.ipynb` intro cell had an orphaned duplicate table fragment** (rows 24–28 rendered twice, once dangling before the real intro paragraph) and a stale `v0.0.25` version string; **`08_agents.ipynb`/`09_hybrid_search.ipynb` fixture/intro text referenced stale `v0.0.17`/`v0.0.18`/`v0.0.23`** version strings predating the project's move to `0.1.x` versioning. All cleaned up.
- Demo docs: `trino-catalog/ailake.properties` comment clarified to avoid conflating Trino's own removed `iceberg.catalog.type=hadoop` connector option with AI-Lake's unrelated `HadoopCatalog` Rust struct (same name, different systems).

- **`migrate_embeddings()` never updated the `ailake.vector-column` table property on cutover, breaking every property-driven reader after a migration** — originally surfaced as `decay-memories` erroring with `vector dimension mismatch: expected N, got 0` on a table that had gone through `add_vector_column` + `backfill_vector_column` + `migrate`; worked around at the time in the demo (`dag_ailake_hook_ops.py`) by keeping the delete/decay table and the schema-evolution table separate. Root-caused to `ailake-query/src/migration.rs`: both `MigrationStrategy::AtomicReplace` and `DualWriteThenCutover` commit their cutover snapshot(s) with `extra_properties: HashMap::new()` — the physical primary vector column is renamed to `new_column` in every rewritten file, but `ailake.vector-column` in the table's properties is never updated to match. Every consumer that resolves "the primary vector column" from that property (not just `decay-memories` — `ailake-cli`'s own `search` command does the identical `meta.properties.get("ailake.vector-column")` lookup when `--vec-col` isn't passed) silently kept querying the old, now-nonexistent column name after any migration — confirmed live: `ailake search` with no `--vec-col` override returned nothing meaningful post-migrate, not just `decay-memories`'s hard error. Fixed by having both strategies' cutover commit(s) merge `{"ailake.vector-column": new_policy.column_name}` into the snapshot's `extra_properties` (a genuine merge per `NewSnapshot`'s own doc comment, not a full property-map replace). Two new regression tests (`dual_write_cutover_updates_vector_column_property`, `atomic_replace_updates_vector_column_property`); verified against the exact live repro (`add_vector_column` → `backfill_vector_column` → `migrate` → `decay-memories`, plus a plain `search` after migrate) via the real `ailake` CLI binary — both now succeed.

- **Data-file names could collide across writer sessions and job re-runs, silently overwriting committed files in place** — full-project audit follow-up to the in-place-rewrite work below; three instances of the same root cause (paths derived from a resettable counter or loop index, no session-unique component):
  - **`TableWriter` part paths (`writer.rs`)** — `create_or_open` seeded the part counter with `list_files().len()`, so any operation that *shrinks* the file count (compaction: 5 files → 1) made the next writer session reuse a retired part's name (`part-00001.parquet` again). Harmless on `HadoopCatalog` (retired bytes already deleted); corrupting under `DuckLakeCatalog`, where the retired file still exists physically *and* is still registered (retention semantics) — the colliding `store.put` rewrote a registered file in place, the exact failure `supports_in_place_rewrite() == false` exists to prevent, and the commit-time guard can't catch it (the path is no longer in the active list). Reproducible with the demo notebook's flow plus one extra insert. Fixed structurally: part paths are now `data/part-<session_ts>-NNNNN.parquet` (writer-construction timestamp + per-session counter) — unique across sessions with no dependence on the current file count; the count-based seeding was removed. Regression test `part_paths_unique_across_sessions_after_compaction` (write 2 parts → simulated compaction Replace → new session write → assert no name reuse).
  - **`BackfillJob` (`backfill.rs`)** — output paths were `data/backfill-{idx}.parquet` with `idx` a plain loop position: a second backfill run (another vector column, or a retry) regenerated the *same* paths and overwrote the committed `backfill-00000.parquet` it was itself reading — on every backend, since backfill never physically deletes old files. Now `data/backfill-<ts>-{idx}.parquet`.
  - **`MigrationJob` (`migration.rs`)** — identical pattern (`data/migrated-{idx}.parquet`; a v2→v3 migration after a v1→v2 one overwrote live files). Now `data/migrated-<ts>-{idx}.parquet`.
- **`MemoryDecayJob` committed snapshots with `parent_snapshot_id: None`** — every decay run broke the table's snapshot lineage (history/time-travel chain), unlike `delete_rows`/`delete_where` which already pass `meta.current_snapshot_id`. Now loads the current snapshot id before committing.

- **In-place data-file rewrites are incompatible with the DuckLake catalog — `MemoryDecayJob` now writes to fresh paths; deferred writes/compaction are refused on that backend** — found extending the demo-notebook verification below into a full audit. DuckLake records each file's zone-map stats *and exact footer size* at `ducklake_add_data_files` time and trusts both afterwards. Two failure modes, both verified against a live extension: (1) a same-length in-place rewrite (the `MemoryDecayJob` shape — `recency_weight` values change, byte length may not) leaves stale zone-maps that silently prune the file out of DuckLake-native filtered reads — `WHERE w > 5` returned 0 with every row at 9.9; (2) a changed-length rewrite (the deferred-index-patch shape — the background build grows the Parquet-only file into a full AILK file at the same path) breaks *every* subsequent native read of the file (`Parquet footer length stored in file is not equal to footer length provided`), including the row-`DELETE` needed to retire it — unrecoverable through sanctioned SQL. Fixes, layered: `CatalogProvider::supports_in_place_rewrite()` (default `true`; `DuckLakeCatalog` returns `false`); `MemoryDecayJob` writes decayed files to fresh `data/decayed-<ts>-<idx>.parquet` paths and retires the old ones on **every** backend (uniform, no DuckLake special-casing; old bytes physically reclaimed only when `retires_files_physically()` allows, same gating as compaction); deferred writes (`TableWriter::write_batch_*_deferred`) and deferred compaction (`CompactionExecutor::run_deferred`) refuse up front on backends returning `false` — the physical in-place patch happens *before* any commit, so a commit-time guard alone would be too late — with the same clear error surfaced by `ailake insert --deferred`/`ailake compact --deferred` at the CLI; and `DuckLakeCatalog::commit_snapshot` hard-errors if a same-path entry arrives with a different `file_size_bytes` than registered (backstop: a size mismatch proves an in-place rewrite already happened). Two new live-extension regression tests (`in_place_rewrite_size_change_rejected`, `rewrite_to_fresh_path_refreshes_stats`); `ailake-catalog`/`ailake-query`/`ailake-cli` suites green (40+85), clippy clean. Design writeup: "In-place rewrites are rejected (and why)" in `docs/guides/DUCKLAKE_CATALOG.md`.

- **`CompactionExecutor` physically deleted retired files even on catalog backends that don't want that yet** — `ailake-query/src/compaction.rs`'s `run`/`run_deferred` unconditionally called `store.delete()` on every file a compaction pass merged away, right after the `Replace` snapshot committed. Correct for manifest-based backends (`HadoopCatalog`/`RestCatalog`/`GlueCatalog`/`JdbcCatalog`/`NessieCatalog`): once a file drops out of the Iceberg manifest, the catalog has no other record of it. Wrong for `DuckLakeCatalog`: its `commit_snapshot` retires a file via a row-predicate `DELETE FROM lake.tbl WHERE filename = ?`, which only attaches a deletion vector — the file stays registered in `ducklake_list_files()` until an operator runs DuckLake's own `ducklake_expire_snapshots`/`ducklake_cleanup_files` (see "The retirement problem" in `docs/guides/DUCKLAKE_CATALOG.md`, added when the backend shipped in 0.1.3). Deleting the bytes immediately left that registration dangling — any subsequent DuckLake-native SQL read touching the file (e.g. a plain `SELECT` through the `ATTACH 'ducklake:...'` connection any external reader would use) failed with `IOException: Cannot open file`. Found by actually running `13_ducklake.ipynb` (new demo notebook, see below) end-to-end against a live `ducklake` extension — not caught by unit tests, since none exercised compaction against `DuckLakeCatalog`. Fixed by adding `CatalogProvider::retires_files_physically() -> bool` (default `true`, preserving existing behavior for all five other backends; `DuckLakeCatalog` overrides to `false`) and gating both `delete_old_files()` call sites in `compaction.rs` on it. Verified: full re-run of the notebook end-to-end (create → insert → evolve → insert-after-evolve → compact → info → direct SQL against both the sidecar and the `lake` attachment, all succeeding) plus the existing `ailake-catalog`/`ailake-query` suites (85 + 38 tests, 0 failures — confirms no behavior change on `HadoopCatalog`).
- **`VectorPrecision::Binary` / `footer::Precision::Binary` removed — dead since v0.0.14** — `docs/specs/FILE_FORMAT.md` §3.1 claimed the `precision=3` column encoding was "still defined... and readers/writers still accept it", but that variant never had a real encoder: `ailake_core::VectorPrecision::Binary`'s size computation and every write path silently fell back to F16 while field metadata still labeled the column `"binary"` (a size mismatch), and no public API (CLI/Python/JNI) ever exposed a way to select it. Removed the `Binary` enum variant from `ailake-core::VectorPrecision` and `ailake-file::footer::Precision`, and its match arms in `ailake-parquet::schema::precision_str`; discriminant `3` kept reserved (not reassigned) in both enums for on-disk forward-compatibility — `TryFrom<u8>` now rejects byte value `3` as invalid instead of silently accepting it as a non-functional encoding. `docs/specs/FILE_FORMAT.md` §3.1 updated to match. Full workspace build + `ailake-core`/`ailake-file`/`ailake-parquet` suites green (42/42).

### Documentation

- **Stale `VectorPrecision`/`VectorMetric` enum listings in `CLAUDE.md` §6B and `docs/architecture/WORKSPACE.md`** — both still listed the `Binary` precision variant (removed in v0.0.14, see above) and a `VectorPrecision::I8Symmetric` name that never existed in `ailake-core::types` (the real variant is `I8`); `VectorMetric` was missing `NormalizedCosine` (added in Fase 6/`pre_normalize`). Found auditing the project after the REST Catalog wiring (Fase 17) landed; both docs now match `ailake-core/src/types.rs` exactly.
- **DuckLake — row-level deletes invisible to native readers** documented as a v1 limitation in `DUCKLAKE_CATALOG.md` (`delete_where`/`delete_rows` live in the sidecar; a plain `SELECT` through the DuckLake attachment still sees deleted rows — asymmetric with file retirement, which native readers do observe), with the possible translate-to-native-`DELETE` fix recorded as a roadmap item in CLAUDE.md.
- **`write_batch_idempotent` retry window after compaction** documented (the `batch_id` tag lives on the `DataFileEntry`; compaction's merged file carries `batch_id: None`, so a retry firing after the batch was compacted away re-inserts it), with the aggregate-batch-ids fix recorded as a roadmap item.
- **`SearchSession` does not filter deleted rows** — docstring now warns that deletion vectors and equality deletes are not applied (unlike `search`/`search_text`); it trades delete visibility for throughput on static snapshots.

### Added

- **Demo — `13_ducklake.ipynb`** — new notebook covering the `DuckLakeCatalog` backend (shipped in 0.1.3 but previously absent from the demo entirely: CLI-only feature, no `ailake-py` binding, so no notebook had touched it). Drives the `ailake` CLI via `subprocess` (create → insert → search → evolve → insert-after-evolve → compact → info), then opens both halves of the catalog directly with `duckdb` — the AI-Lake sidecar (`ailake_vector_index`) and the real DuckLake attachment (`ATTACH 'ducklake:...'`) — to make the two-tier design concrete. `tests/docker/demo/Dockerfile` now builds `ailake-cli --features catalog-ducklake` (needs `cmake` for `duckdb`'s bundled C++ build) into the demo image; `tests/docker/compose-demo.yml` gained `DEMO_DUCKLAKE_STORE`. Build time for the demo image increases from ~3-5 min to ~8-12 min cold as a result — documented in `docs/guides/DEMO_NOTEBOOKS.md`.
- **Demo — closed three Fase 15 (`ailake-py`) coverage gaps in existing notebooks**, found auditing the demo against the current SDK surface: `01_ailake_demo.ipynb` §17 now calls the native `ailake.estimate()` binding instead of a hand-rolled reimplementation of the same math; §12 gained a `rerank_factor` demo (exact-distance reranking after IVF-PQ, compared against brute-force ground truth); `10_gpu_demo.ipynb` §3 switched from the heuristic-driven `write_batch_auto_deferred` to the actually-forced `write_batch_ivf_pq`/`write_batch_ivf_pq_deferred` (the section's own markdown already claimed to "force each engine explicitly," but the code silently depended on hardware heuristics that could pick HNSW on <8-core machines); `08_agents.ipynb` gained a §4b demonstrating `ailake.TimestampNs` + native `decay_memories()` and fixed a stale "MemoryDecayJob (Phase 9, pending)" claim (it shipped in 0.1.2).

## [0.1.4] — 2026-07-14

### Added

- **`docs/guides/CLI_INTEGRATION.md`** — new dedicated guide for the `ailake-cli` binary, covering every subcommand with real captured output. All 6 existing integration guides audited and updated against current source.

- **Demo — `13_ducklake.ipynb`** — new notebook covering the `DuckLakeCatalog` backend. Drives the `ailake` CLI via `subprocess` (create → insert → search → evolve → compact → info), then opens both halves of the catalog directly with `duckdb`.

- **Demo — closed three Fase 15 (`ailake-py`) coverage gaps** in existing notebooks: native `ailake.estimate()`, `rerank_factor` after IVF-PQ, forced `write_batch_ivf_pq*` calls, `TimestampNs` + `decay_memories()` demo.

### Fixed

- **In-place data-file rewrites incompatible with DuckLake catalog** — `MemoryDecayJob` now writes fresh `data/decayed-<ts>-<idx>.parquet` paths; deferred writes/compaction refused on `DuckLakeCatalog`.

- **`CompactionExecutor` physically deleted retired files even on backends that don't want that** — added `CatalogProvider::retires_files_physically() -> bool`; `DuckLakeCatalog` returns `false`.

- **`MemoryDecayJob` committed snapshots with `parent_snapshot_id: None`** — breaking the snapshot lineage chain. Now loads current snapshot ID before committing.

- **Session-unique data-file paths** — part paths, `BackfillJob`, and `MigrationJob` output now include a timestamp component (`part-<ts>-NNNNN.parquet`), preventing name collision across sessions.

- **Trino plugin `SELECT` execution — two bugs** (`NullPointerException` reconstructing `VectorScanTableHandle`, `IllegalAccessException` on `VectorScanTransactionHandle`). Both confirmed fixed against live Trino 430 server.

- **`ailake delete-where` silently did nothing** — `EqualityDeleteFile.path` was double-prefixed with `table_root`, resulting in a 404 on read. Fixed by passing a `table_root`-relative path instead.

- **Demo notebook fixes** — `assemble_context()` return value handling, IVF-PQ `rerank_factor` cell, `os.environ.get("QUERY_PATH")` bug, orphaned duplicate table fragment, stale version strings.

## [0.1.3] — 2026-07-10

### Added

- **`ailake-catalog` — capability parity audit across all 6 `CatalogProvider` backends** — same audit pattern as the JVM/CLI/SDK parity sweeps (Fases 11-15), applied to the catalog layer itself: `HadoopCatalog`, `RestCatalog`, `GlueCatalog`, `NessieCatalog`, `JdbcCatalog`, `DuckLakeCatalog`. Found `evolve_schema`/`list_equality_deletes` silently falling back to the trait's own defaults (unsupported / empty) on 4 of 6 backends, and — the actually serious one — `commit_snapshot` on Rest/Glue/Jdbc never referencing `snapshot.equality_delete_files` at all, meaning `delete_rows` against those three backends silently did nothing: no error, no data change, deleted rows stayed fully visible in search results. Closed in six phases:
  - **Fase 0 (the silent-drop bug)** — `crate::snapshot::Manifest` (the flat JSON manifest Rest/Glue/Jdbc used at the time) gained an `equality_delete_files` field (`#[serde(default)]`, old manifests still parse); `commit_snapshot` on all three now persists it, accumulating across `Append`/`Delete` commits and replacing on `Overwrite`/`Replace` — the same contract already established for `files`.
  - **Fase 1** — real `evolve_schema` (actual `metadata.json` schema-field patch, mirroring `HadoopCatalog`'s existing logic exactly) on Rest (via REST `add-schema`/`set-current-schema` updates), Glue (version-id-guarded `update_table` retry), Jdbc (CAS `UPDATE ... WHERE metadata_location = old` retry). `add_vector_column`'s default trait impl calls `evolve_schema`, so it started working on all three for free. `NessieCatalog` needed its own explicit delegation added too — Rust doesn't forward trait methods automatically just because a struct wraps another implementor.
  - **Fase 2** — real `list_equality_deletes` reading back what Fase 0 now writes.
  - **Fase 3** — `RestCatalog::create_table` was silently ignoring `format_version`/`partition_column_type`/`partition_fields` entirely (hardcoded V1 properties, empty schema, no partition spec) — now reuses `IcebergMetadata::new` (the same schema/partition-spec/properties construction every other backend already uses) and issues a follow-up `upgrade-format-version` REST update for V3 (not a field `CreateTableRequest` accepts per the spec's own OpenAPI schema — confirmed by downloading and reading `apache/iceberg`'s `rest-catalog-open-api.yaml` directly rather than guessing).
  - **Fase 5** — `RestCatalog::commit_snapshot`/`evolve_schema` now send real OCC `requirements` (`assert-ref-snapshot-id`, `assert-current-schema-id`) with a retry×5 loop on 409, matching the CAS/version-id retry pattern Glue/Jdbc already had. Previously sent `requirements: []` unconditionally — any two concurrent writers could silently clobber each other's commits with no conflict detection at all.
  - **Fase 4 (the big one)** — Rest/Glue/Jdbc's `commit_snapshot`/`list_files`/`list_equality_deletes` never actually adopted the real Iceberg Avro-manifest format `snapshot.rs`'s own header comment had flagged as "Phase 2" back when `HadoopCatalog` got it — they stayed on a flat single-JSON-file-per-snapshot manifest indefinitely, missing V3 `first_row_id` row-lineage assignment, Phase F Puffin stats (vector centroids + BM25 blooms), and Phase J partition-stats Parquet entirely. Extracted `HadoopCatalog`'s ~320-line `commit_snapshot` (plus its manifest-reading logic) into a new shared `ailake-catalog/src/manifest_commit.rs` module so every backend calls the *exact* logic Hadoop does instead of a hand-rolled approximation that could silently drift from it. Split into two layers specifically so Rest could reuse it too (see the next bullet): `build_commit()` writes the real Avro manifest(s) + Puffin/partition-stats files and returns a `CommitArtifacts` bundle without touching any metadata struct; `apply_commit()` folds that bundle into an owned `IcebergMetadata` in place (what Hadoop/Glue/Jdbc persist); `commit_into_metadata()` is the `build_commit`+`apply_commit` convenience wrapper those three backends actually call. `HadoopCatalog` itself was refactored to call the extracted functions, verified against its own pre-existing test suite (6 tests, including the V3 `first_row_id` monotonicity and Replace-doesn't-inherit-manifest regression tests) with zero behavior change. `list_files` data-file paths are now **absolute** on Glue/Jdbc (Iceberg spec requirement, matching Hadoop) rather than warehouse-relative, since manifests now go through the real Avro writer. `GlueCatalog` has no live-AWS test coverage (same as before this work); `JdbcCatalog` got new real-SQLite coverage for `evolve_schema` and equality-delete accumulation added to its existing end-to-end test.
  - **Fase 4b (Rest/Nessie follow-up, same session)** — `RestCatalog::commit_snapshot` now calls `build_commit()` directly and translates the returned `CommitArtifacts` into REST protocol `TableUpdate`s instead of writing the flat JSON manifest: `add-snapshot`/`set-snapshot-ref` for the real Avro-manifest-backed snapshot, `add-schema`/`set-current-schema`/`set-properties` for the Phase G/I schema patch, and two new update variants — `set-statistics`/`set-partition-statistics` — for the Phase F Puffin stats and Phase J partition-stats refs, mapped field-for-field onto the REST spec's own `StatisticsFile`/`PartitionStatisticsFile` schemas (verified against `apache/iceberg`'s `rest-catalog-open-api.yaml`, including the `blob-metadata` key name already pinned to match it in `metadata.rs`). The REST spec has no update to correct an existing partition spec's `source-id` in place (Phase I's remap case) — handled instead via `add-spec`+`set-default-spec` (register the corrected spec as new, make it default), the spec-correct equivalent. `next-row-id` needs no explicit update at all — the spec's own field description says the server derives it from `first_row_id`/`record_count` already present in the manifest, which `build_commit` already assigns correctly. `list_files`/`list_equality_deletes` now read the real Avro manifest via the same shared `list_files_from_metadata`/`list_equality_deletes_from_metadata` Hadoop/Glue/Jdbc use, replacing the flat-JSON read path entirely. `NessieCatalog` inherits all of this for free (pure delegation to `RestCatalog`). No live REST server available to test against in this environment — verified via compilation + the existing unit test suite (54 tests) + the shared `build_commit` logic already being proven correct through Hadoop/Glue/Jdbc's real tests; the REST-specific `CommitArtifacts` → `TableUpdate` translation itself is new and untested against a live server.

- **`ailake-catalog` — `DuckLakeCatalog` backend (Fase 5, queued item closed)** — new `CatalogProvider` implementation (`catalog-ducklake` feature) storing AI-Lake table metadata in a real [DuckLake](https://ducklake.select) catalog, driven entirely through the real DuckDB `ducklake` extension (`INSTALL ducklake; LOAD ducklake; ATTACH 'ducklake:...'`) rather than hand-rolled catalog DDL — the DuckLake bootstrap/versioning invariants aren't fully public, so this backend never writes to DuckLake's own tables directly, only sanctioned SQL (`CREATE`/`ALTER`/`DROP TABLE`, `CALL ducklake_add_data_files(...)`, `ducklake_list_files(...)`, row-predicate `DELETE`). AI-Lake's own per-file vector metadata (centroid, radius, HNSW offset/len, index status, etc.) lives in a sidecar table (`main.ailake_vector_index`) outside the DuckLake attachment, since it has no home in DuckLake's fixed schema.
  - Full `Append`/`Overwrite`/`Replace`/`Delete` support (diffs old-vs-new file lists, retires/adds as needed) — same operations `compaction.rs`/`backfill.rs`/`memory_decay.rs`/`migration.rs`/`writer.rs`'s deferred-index-status patch all depend on. `evolve_schema` maps to real `ALTER TABLE ADD/RENAME COLUMN`.
  - Two real bugs found and fixed against a **live** `ducklake` extension (not just docs) during implementation, both documented in `docs/guides/DUCKLAKE_CATALOG.md`: (1) DuckDB refuses to write to two attached databases in one transaction ("a single transaction can only write to a single attached database") — `commit_snapshot`/`evolve_schema` now commit in two sequential phases (`lake` then sidecar) instead of one atomic transaction, with a documented graceful-degradation story for a crash between the two; (2) row-predicate `DELETE FROM lake.tbl WHERE filename = ?` correctly empties a file's rows for any DuckLake reader but does **not** remove it from `ducklake_list_files()` (only a maintenance pass does) — `list_files()` was redesigned around the sidecar's own `active` flag as the authority for exclusion, with `ducklake_list_files()` used only to detect genuinely foreign (non-AI-Lake-written) files.
  - Wired into `ailake-cli` behind its own opt-in `catalog-ducklake` feature (not part of the default build — it pulls in `duckdb`'s bundled C++ build): new `--catalog hadoop|ducklake` global flag, defaults to `hadoop` (unchanged behavior). `ducklake` only supports a local filesystem `--store`, erroring clearly (not falling back silently) on `s3://`/`gs://`/`az://` or when the binary was built without the feature. `JdbcCatalog`/`GlueCatalog`/`NessieCatalog` remain backend-only, not wired into any CLI/Python surface — DuckLake's embedded, connection-string-free nature is what makes a single flag a reasonable CLI surface for it specifically, unlike the others.
  - CLI wiring surfaced two more real bugs verified end-to-end (create → insert → evolve → insert-after-evolve → search → compact → info) against the built binary, not just unit tests: relative `DataFileEntry::path` (warehouse-relative, the convention every backend uses) was never resolved to an absolute filesystem path before being handed to `ducklake_add_data_files`/the `filename` DELETE predicate, failing the very first real `ailake insert`; and `ducklake_add_data_files` needed `allow_missing => true` in addition to `ignore_extra_columns => true`, or any file inserted after `evolve_schema` added a column (the normal case) was rejected outright.
  - Tested with a real round-trip (no mocks) against a live DuckDB/DuckLake catalog file: create → insert → search-shaped list → Overwrite (the compaction/backfill pattern: retire one file, add another) → `evolve_schema` → drop.
### Fixed

- **`ParquetVectorReader::read_all()` (`ailake-parquet`) always decoded the vector column as F16, ignoring the file's actual stored precision** — found while verifying `ailake compact` against a table created with `--precision f32` (surfaced through the new DuckLake CLI wiring above, but reproduces identically with the default `HadoopCatalog` — a pre-existing bug independent of catalog backend). Every AI-Lake writer embeds `ailake.precision` in the Parquet file's own KV metadata, but the reader — used by `AilakeFileReader::read_parquet()`, the path both compaction and the scanner's foreign-file flat scan go through — never read it back, unconditionally decoding via `Quantizer::f16_bytes_to_f32` (2 bytes/element). For any F32-precision table (4 bytes/element), this silently produced a `Vec<f32>` of the wrong length, surfacing as a `debug_assert_eq!` panic in `ailake-vec::cosine_distance` (`dimension mismatch 8 vs 4` for `dim=4`) in debug builds — and would have silently misbehaved instead of panicking in release, where the assert compiles out. Fixed by reading `ailake.precision` from the file's own KV metadata and decoding accordingly (new `Quantizer::f32_bytes_to_f32`; `f16`/`f32` supported, other precisions now error clearly instead of silently misreading — I8's scaling params aren't persisted anywhere to reconstruct exact values from raw bytes, a separate pre-existing gap not addressed here). Absent `ailake.precision` (raw external source files fed to `ailake insert`, which predate any AI-Lake writer touching them) still defaults to F16, preserving that path's documented contract. Affects any F32-precision table run through `ailake compact` — not a synthetic-test-only or DuckLake-specific bug. Verified with a full workspace test run (294 passed) plus a real before/after repro via the built CLI binary (`ailake compact` on a `--precision f32` table: panicked before, compacts cleanly and returns correct distances after).

## [0.1.2] — 2026-07-10

### Added

- **`ailake-py` — capability parity audit + fixes (Fase 15)** — same audit pattern as Fase 12/13/14, applied to the Python (PyO3) SDK. Unlike the previous audits, most findings here were correctness bugs in already-existing bindings (silently wrong behavior, not just missing coverage):
  - **`assemble_context()` dedup was permanently dead** — the PyO3 binding hardcoded `embedding: None` on every chunk regardless of input, so `ContextAssembler`'s cosine-distance dedup loop was always a no-op for any `dedup_threshold` value. Fixed by accepting an optional `"embedding"` key per chunk dict. Also now exposes `group_by_document`/`max_chunks_per_document` (previously hardcoded via `..Default::default()`) and returns `{"text", "chunk_count", "token_estimate"}` instead of a bare string (breaking change — `Agent.assemble_context()` updated to unwrap `["text"]`, preserving its own str-returning contract).
