  - **`search(..., fetch_data=True)` silently dropped `hybrid_text`/`text_column`/`bm25_weight`/`ef_search`/`pruning_threshold`/`rerank_factor`** — the underlying `search_with_data`/`_search_with_data` pyfunction only ever accepted `(path, query, top_k, partition_filter)`, unlike its sibling `search()` (pointer-only mode) which fully supported all of them. The same `SearchQuery` object silently returned different result sets depending on whether `.to_list()` or `.to_pandas()` was called. Fixed by giving `search_with_data` full parameter parity with `search()`; also newly exposed on `search_multimodal()` (`ef_search`, `pruning_threshold`) and as `rerank_factor` everywhere (was hardcoded `None` in all three search functions, so IVF-PQ tables never got the exact-reranking correction pass that `ailake_query::scanner::SearchConfig::rerank_factor` exists specifically for).
  - **`now_ns()`'s own documented use produced a column `decay_memories()` rejects** — `now_ns()`'s docstring instructs writing its return value into `last_accessed_at`/`created_at` via `extra_columns`, but `build_batch_with_extra` had no `Timestamp` branch (only bool/float/int64/string inferred from the first Python value), so a plain `int` became `Int64` — a type `ailake_query::memory_decay::days_old_vec` explicitly rejects (`PyValueError: last_accessed_at must be Timestamp(Nanosecond/Microsecond) or Utf8`), crashing every subsequent `decay_memories()` call on that table. Fixed with a new `ailake.TimestampNs(ns: int)` wrapper class recognized by `build_batch_with_extra`, producing a real `Timestamp(Nanosecond, UTC)` Arrow column.
  - **`Agent` was incompatible with the rest of the ecosystem and with `decay_memories()`** — `remember()`/`log_tool_call()` packed all metadata (`agent_id`, `importance`, `last_accessed_at`, `tool_name`, etc.) as a JSON blob prefixed onto the `text` column instead of real typed columns, so (a) tables written via `Agent` were opaque single-text-column blobs to every other AI-Lake client (Spark/Trino/Flink/DuckDB/CLI), and (b) `decay_memories()` found no real `last_accessed_at` column in any file, silently skipped every file, and permanently returned `0` — no error, just a job that never did anything. `Agent.recall()` also reimplemented its own recency decay in pure Python using `time.time()` (seconds) rather than `now_ns()` (nanoseconds) — two parallel, non-interoperating recency mechanisms. Rewrote `remember()`/`log_tool_call()`/`recall()` to write and read real typed columns (`agent_id`, `session_id`, `step_index`, `mem_type`, `record_id`, `importance`, `created_at`/`last_accessed_at` as `TimestampNs`, `access_count`, `tool_name`, `tool_input_json`, `tool_output_json`, `outcome`, `latency_ms`) matching `EpisodicMemorySchema`/`ToolCallSchema`'s field names — `decay_memories()` now works directly against `Agent`-written tables, and the table is queryable by any other AI-Lake client. `recall()`'s public return-dict contract (`mem_id`/`call_id`, `type`, `score`, etc.) is unchanged.
  - **`compact()` bypassed the native binding entirely, shelling out to a separately-installed CLI binary** — despite `ailake_query::compaction` already being linked into `ailake-py`, the pure-Python `compact()` used `subprocess.run([...])` against `$AILAKE_BIN`/`PATH`-resolved `ailake`, silently returning `{"ok": true, "files_compacted": 0, "warning": "..."}` when the binary wasn't found — `"ok": true"` reads as success, so a caller checking only `files_compacted > 0` would conclude "nothing to compact" rather than "the tool never ran." Replaced with a native `compact()` PyO3 function calling `CompactionPlanner`/`CompactionExecutor` directly (mirroring `ailake-cli`'s own `Compact` handler); also fixed `target_size_bytes`'s default, which diverged from the CLI's own default (128 MiB vs. the CLI's 512 MiB) — now `536_870_912` in both.
  - **`add_vector_column`/`backfill_vector_column` compiled into the native module but unreachable from `import ailake`** — both fully implemented and registered in `_ailake` (mirroring `ailake-cli`'s `AddVectorColumn`/`BackfillVectorColumn` 1:1) but missing from `__init__.py`'s import list, `__all__`, and the `.pyi` stub — `ailake.add_vector_column(...)` raised `AttributeError`, and IDEs/type-checkers never suggested it existed. Now exported.
  - **`write_batch_ivf_pq`/`write_batch_ivf_pq_deferred` had zero PyO3 wrapper** — Python users had no way to force IVF-PQ indexing (only the hardware/batch-size heuristic in `write_batch_auto_deferred`). Added both as `TableWriter` methods.
  - **`write_batch_multi`/`write_batch_multi_deferred` had no `extra_columns`** — unlike `write_batch`/`write_batch_auto_deferred`, the multi-column write path hardcoded a single `text` column with no way to also write `MultimodalContextSchema` companion columns (`media_uri`, `media_caption`, etc.) in the same call. Added `extra_columns` param (reuses `build_batch_with_extra`, which also gave this path the same `TimestampNs`/type-inference support as the single-column path for free).
  - **`VectorColSpec` couldn't set per-column `precision`/`pre_normalize`/`hnsw_m`/`hnsw_ef_construction`** — every secondary column in a multi-column write always got `VectorStoragePolicy::default_f16(...)` regardless of what the primary column or `add_vector_column` (which already exposes exactly these knobs) would allow. Added all four fields to `VectorColSpec`.
  - **No `scan()` — `ailake_scan_json` (ailake-jni) had no ailake-py equivalent** — turned out `search_with_data()` already *is* that capability (search + full-row fetch, no JOIN needed), just under a different name; added `ailake.scan` as a naming-parity alias (matches `ailake-go`'s `Scan()`), not a reimplementation.
  - **No `estimate()`** — `ailake-cli`'s `Estimate` subcommand (pure math, no I/O) had no Python equivalent at all, not even a subprocess-based fallback like `compact()`'s old design. Added a native `estimate()` mirroring the CLI's math exactly (6 storage-precision-mode rows: F32/F16/I8, ±IVF-PQ, PQ-only).
  - **`Table` (the "recommended" fluent API) was missing `write_batch_idempotent`/`write_batch_multi`/`write_batch_multi_deferred`** — present only on the lower-level `TableWriter`, forcing users who needed idempotent or multimodal writes to drop the fluent API entirely for that code path. Added matching `Table` methods.
  - **Stale `.pyi` stub declared a fictional `Agent` class** with `agent_id`/`session_id` `@property` accessors and a `str`-returning `assemble_context()` that never matched the real (pure-Python, `__init__.py`-defined, privately-attributed) `Agent` class — `Agent`/`Table`/`SearchQuery` are not part of the compiled `_ailake` extension at all and don't belong in this stub file. Removed the fictional block; added stubs for `TimestampNs`, `compact`, `estimate`, `add_vector_column`, `backfill_vector_column`, and updated every signature touched above (`search`, `search_with_data`, `search_multimodal`, `assemble_context`, `VectorColSpec`, `write_batch_multi*`).
  - **Zero test coverage for `ailake-py`** — explains why the dead-dedup, dropped-params, and Timestamp-crash bugs above shipped undetected; the only existing check was a single compat script with no `pytest` infrastructure. Added `ailake-py/tests/test_capability_parity.py` (16 tests, real `maturin develop` build, no mocks) covering every fix above; wired into the existing `compat-ailake-py` CI job. Also updated `tests/compat/check_ailake_py.py`'s `assemble_context` assertions for the new dict return shape and real dedup behavior (was asserting against a bare string with a `dedup_threshold` param that provably did nothing).
  - Verified with a real `maturin develop --release` build against a real venv (Python 3.14, pyarrow 24, no pandas — caught a real `pyarrow.TimestampScalar.as_py()` nanosecond-resolution limitation along the way, worked around with `.value` instead), the new 16-test pytest suite, the full pre-existing `tests/compat/check_ailake_py.py` (60+ checks, 0 regressions), `mypy --ignore-missing-imports --no-strict-optional` (0 errors), and `cargo clippy --release -p ailake-py` (0 warnings). Docs updated: `ailake-py/README.md`, `ailake-py/python/ailake/_ailake.pyi`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `CLAUDE.md` (Fase 15).

- **`ailake-go`/`ailake-cpp` — capability parity audit + fixes (Fase 14)** — same audit pattern as Fase 12 (JVM plugins) and Fase 13 (CLI/DuckDB/Airflow), applied to the two native SDK clients. Both bundle a mix of pure reimplementation (reads: `Search`, `Scan`, `SearchMultimodal`) and CLI-delegation (writes/deletes/evolve) — `ailake-go` because it's pure-Go with no cgo, `ailake-cpp` because it's deliberately header-only with no Rust FFI at the C++ layer. Found real capability gaps (every other CLI-backed op already had a wrapper, these two didn't) plus, while setting up real end-to-end verification for the new C++ functions, five separate pre-existing correctness bugs in `ailake-cpp`'s catalog/Avro-reading path that silently broke every real (non-mocked) read against a table written by this project's own CLI:
  - **`ailake-cli insert` was also missing `--metric`/`--precision`/`--embedding-model`** — a third occurrence of the exact bug class fixed in Fase 13 for the Airflow provider: both `ailake-go`'s `WriteBatch` and `ailake-cpp`'s `write_batch` already send these three flags unconditionally when set, but `Insert` never accepted them. Extended the CLI to match, same fix pattern as before.
  - **`ailake-go` — `Compact` + multi-column `WriteBatch`** — new `Compact(catalog, ns, table, opts)` (requests `--format json` from the CLI from the start, avoiding the exact "text output has no parseable count" bug found in `AilakeHook.compact()` during Fase 13); `WriteBatchOptions` gained `VectorCols []VectorColSpec` — when set, builds `--vector-cols col:dim:metric[:modality],...` instead of `--embeddings`, wiring up the CLI's existing multi-column (Phase 8 multimodal) insert path that `ailake-go` never exposed.
  - **`ailake-go` — pre-existing path double-prefix bug** — `resolveAvroPath` (catalog.go) and `searchFile`/`searchFileCol`'s file resolution (ailake.go, multimodal.go) incorrectly re-joined already-warehouse-root-relative paths (from `manifest_list`/`DataFileEntry.path`, which the Rust `HadoopCatalog` always stores relative to the warehouse root, already including namespace/table) against the table directory a second time — producing broken paths like `.../warehouse/default/media/default/media/metadata/....avro`. Genuinely pre-existing, reproducible with unmodified `WriteBatch`/`Search`, not caused by the new code; fixed all 3 call sites to join against the warehouse root only, matching the already-correct pattern in `scan.go`'s `FetchRows`.
  - **`ailake-cpp` — `write_batch_multi` + `compact`** — new `ailake::write_batch_multi(warehouse, table_id, parquet, vector_cols, opts)` and `ailake::compact(warehouse, table_id, opts)`, mirroring the Go additions and the existing `write_batch`/`delete_where`/`evolve_schema` CLI-shell-out pattern in `write.hpp`. `compact` parses `"files_compacted":N` from `--format json` output via substring search (no JSON dependency in this header-only file, same style as `evolve_schema`'s `new_schema_id` parse).
  - **`ailake-cpp` — five pre-existing catalog/Avro bugs found and fixed while verifying the above against a real table** (none caused by the new code; all reproducible with unmodified `search`/`list_files`):
    - `table_dir()` used a Hive-style `<ns>.db/<tbl>` layout that appears nowhere else in the project; the real on-disk layout (confirmed against `HadoopCatalog::table_root()` in Rust) is flat `<ns>/<tbl>` — would have made `load_table`/`list_files` fail to find any table this project's own CLI ever wrote.
    - `resolve_path()` and `list_files()` double-joined already-warehouse-relative manifest/data-file paths against the table dir a second time — the same double-prefix bug independently found in `ailake-go`.
    - `detail::read_zigzag()` had no EOF/failure check on the underlying stream read, so a failed read spun forever on uninitialized stack garbage — an infinite hang (found via `strace`, root-caused by comparing against `write_avro_container` in `ailake-catalog/src/avro_raw.rs`, which never emits a trailing `count=0` terminator). Now throws `std::runtime_error` on read failure, and both manifest readers treat a clean EOF at a block boundary as a normal loop exit rather than an error.
    - Avro OCF data blocks always encode `count, byte_size, objects, sync`, but the reader only read `byte_size` when `count` was negative — a convention that actually belongs to generic array/map fields, not top-level manifest data blocks. Manifest parsing was silently misaligned by 4 bytes per file. Fixed in both `read_manifest_list` and `read_manifest_file`.
    - `read_manifest_file()` was missing a skip for the trailing `first_row_id: union<null,long>` field that Rust's `write_manifest_file()` always encodes (V3 row lineage, null for V2 tables) — misaligning every record by one field.
    - `parse_key_metadata()` assumed `centroid_b64` packed `dim + 1` floats with the last one being `radius`; in reality `radius` is a separate top-level JSON field (`AilakeEntryExt::radius`), so the centroid was silently truncated by one dimension (causing a dim mismatch against the query vector) and radius was decoded from garbage bytes.
    - `search_file()` treated the manifest's `hnsw_offset` as the position of the AILK *header*, but it's actually already the absolute offset of the index *blob* itself (`ailk_start + header.hnsw_offset` per `writer.rs`/`compaction.rs`) — reading the header from the wrong file offset and computing the wrong blob position. Now back-computes the header position by subtracting header + centroid/radius size, matching `ailake-go`'s already-correct `searchFileAtOffset`.
    - `list_files()`'s `current-snapshot-id` extraction used a hardcoded `+= 23` offset for a 22-character key, silently dropping the leading digit of the snapshot ID on every call; its manifest-list lookup then used a bare substring search for that (already-wrong) numeric ID anywhere in the file, which only "worked" by accident for single-snapshot tables (via partial-substring containment) and broke outright for any table with snapshot history (e.g. post-compaction), always resolving to the *first* snapshot in the array instead of the current one. Rewrote as a depth-aware walk of the `snapshots` array matching the exact (whitespace-tolerant) `snapshot-id` field.
  - Combined effect: `search()`/`search_multimodal()` against any real multi-row or multi-snapshot `ailake-cpp` table previously returned zero results or the wrong file's rows — a correctness bug in the read path, not just a missing-feature gap.
  - Explicitly out of scope (documented, not fixed): `ailake-cpp`'s `scan` gap. Unlike `ailake-go` (which bundles `github.com/parquet-go/parquet-go` for its native full-row `Scan`), `ailake-cpp` is deliberately header-only with no Parquet-reading dependency; adding `scan` needs either a new dependency (conflicts with the design) or a CLI `scan` subcommand that doesn't exist yet — same missing-CLI-surface blocker already flagged out of scope in the Fase 13 audit.
  - **Verified with real builds and real running binaries, not mocks**: `ailake-go` — `go build ./...`, `go vet ./...`, and a real round-trip (`WriteBatch` with 2 `VectorColSpec`s against `target/debug/ailake`, `SearchMultimodal` returning real RRF-fused results, `Compact` after 2 batches merging to 1 file with all rows still searchable), plus the full 83+ existing test suite. `ailake-cpp` — `cmake --build` + `ctest` (all 5 suites green), and a real end-to-end round-trip against `target/debug/ailake`: `write_batch_multi` → `search_multimodal` (3 RRF results), two `write_batch` calls → `compact` (1 file compacted) → `search` (all 12 rows across both original batches still searchable) — each of the 7 catalog/Avro bugs above was found and fixed by iterating this exact round-trip via `strace`-level debugging until real results came back correct, not by code review alone.

- **`ailake-cli`/`duckdb-ailake`/`airflow-providers-ailake` — capability parity audit across the CLI, DuckDB extension, and Airflow provider** — mirroring the Fase 12 JVM-plugin parity audit, compared `ailake-cli`'s subcommands and `duckdb-ailake`'s SQL functions against the native `ailake-jni`/`ailake-query` capability surface, and the Airflow provider's hook/operator coverage against the CLI. Found one active correctness bug (not just missing coverage) plus several genuine gaps:
  - **`ailake-cli insert` was missing 8 flags** (`--partition-by`, `--partition-value`, `--partition-fields`, `--format-version`, `--hnsw-m`, `--hnsw-ef`, `--pre-normalize`, `--deferred`) that `ailake_write_batch_json` (used by every JVM plugin and `ailake-py`) already accepts per-write — `partition_by`/`partition_value`/`partition_fields` didn't exist as CLI flags on *any* command; the rest existed only on `Create`, not `Insert`. Any `airflow-providers-ailake` DAG setting any of these on `AilakeWriteOperator` crashed at runtime with a clap "unexpected argument" error — the provider was written against the intended capability surface, not the CLI's actual (incomplete) one. Fixed by extending `Insert`'s flags to match `ailake_write_batch_json`'s `Req` struct, threaded through both the single-column and multi-column (`--vector-cols`) policy construction. `--deferred` is mutually exclusive with `--batch-id` on the CLI (deferred writes don't carry an idempotency tag yet); `AilakeWriteOperator` now drops `batch_id` with a warning instead of crashing when `deferred=True`.
  - **New `ailake decay-memories <table> --lambda <λ>` subcommand** — `AilakeHook.decay_memories()` called this subcommand under the assumption it existed; it didn't (`ailake-py`'s PyO3 binding and `MemoryDecayJob` existed, but no CLI wrapper), so every call failed. New subcommand mirrors `ailake-py`'s `decay_memories` binding, prints `files_updated: N` matching the hook's existing parser.
  - **`duckdb-ailake` — `ailake_write_batch_multi` and `ailake_compact`** — 2 of 9 native capabilities were never wired into a DuckDB SQL function (no `.cpp`, no dlsym, no test). New `ailake_write_batch_multi(table_path, ids, vector_columns)` scalar function (`vector_columns` is a `LIST(STRUCT(col, dim, embeddings, metric, precision, modality))`, same STRUCT-list idiom as `ailake_search_multimodal`) and `ailake_compact(table_path, min_files:=..., target_size_bytes:=..., ...)`, both following the established arity-overload-ladder pattern (`ailake_write_batch`/`ailake_delete_where`). New `AilakeLib::write_batch_multi`/`AilakeLib::compact` C++ methods in `ailake_extension.cpp`. New tests `test_write_multi.py`/`test_compact.py`, wired into `ci-duckdb.yml`.
  - **`airflow-providers-ailake` — 6 CLI-supported-but-never-wrapped capabilities** — new `AilakeHook.migrate`/`delete_rows`/`add_vector_column`/`backfill_vector_column`/`estimate` methods and matching `AilakeMigrateOperator`/`AilakeDeleteRowsOperator`/`AilakeAddVectorColumnOperator`/`AilakeBackfillVectorColumnOperator` operators; `AilakeWriteOperator` gained `vector_cols` (multimodal insert, `--vector-cols`); `AilakeCompactOperator`/`AilakeHook.compact` gained `max_files_per_pass`. `delete_rows` requires `format_version=3` (Iceberg Deletion Vectors are V3-only) — documented on both the hook method and the operator, verified with a real error message on a V2 table and a real success on a V3 table.
  - **Also fixed while auditing `compact`**: `AilakeHook.compact()` never requested `--format json`, so its `"files_compacted:"` text-substring parser could never match the CLI's actual text-mode output (`"compacted into <path>"` / `"nothing to compact..."`) — it silently always returned `0` regardless of the real result. Now requests `--format json` and parses the `files_compacted` field, same convention as `get_table_info`.
  - Explicitly out of scope (flagged, not fixed): `search_multimodal` (cross-modal RRF) and `ailake_scan_json` (no-JOIN full-row fetch) exist in the Rust query layer and JNI but were never wired into `ailake-cli` at all — closing this needs real CLI output-format design work (arbitrary-column JSON rows, multimodal query syntax on a command line) beyond a mechanical wire-up.
  - **Verified with real builds and real CLI/extension calls, not just unit tests**: `cargo build -p ailake-cli` + a manual round-trip (`insert --hnsw-m 32 --pre-normalize --format-version 3 --partition-by ... `, `decay-memories`) confirmed the new flags are actually persisted in `metadata.json`. DuckDB extension built via `cmake --build` and loaded into a real DuckDB session (`sys.setdlopenflags(RTLD_GLOBAL)` before `import duckdb`, matching the existing test scripts' documented trick) — `ailake_write_batch_multi` → `ailake_search_multimodal` → `ailake_compact` round-tripped a real 2-column table, merged 2 files into 1, and kept all 5 rows searchable; all 8 pre-existing `duckdb-ailake` test files (48 cases) still pass. Airflow: installed `apache-airflow` + `pytest` in a venv, ran the full existing 60-test suite (0 regressions) plus 22 new tests covering every new hook method/operator and both bug fixes; additionally drove `AilakeHook`/`AilakeWriteOperator` directly against the real `target/debug/ailake` binary (not mocked) for `migrate`, `add_vector_column`, `backfill_vector_column`, `decay_memories`, `compact`, `estimate`, and `delete_rows` (both the V2-rejection error path and the V3 success path).

- **`spark-plugin`/`trino-plugin`/`ailake-flink` — full capability parity across all three JVM plugins (Fase 12)** — audit comparing all 11 native `ailake-jni` capabilities against each plugin's SQL/DataFrame surface found Trino and Flink near-parity (10/11) but Spark missing 5 with zero DataFrame caller despite full native implementation in `AilakeNative.scala` (real dead code — unlike ALTER TABLE, which used to throw `UnsupportedOperationException` explicitly), plus a symmetric gap: multi-column (multimodal) write existed only in Spark. Closed:
  - **Spark — hybrid BM25+vector search**: `ailakeSearch` gained `hybridText`/`textColumn`/`bm25Weight` params (already existed on `AilakeNative.search`, never threaded through by the only DataFrame caller).
  - **Spark — pure full-text search**: `implicits.AilakeSession.ailakeSearchText(tableUri, queryText, ...)`.
  - **Spark — DELETE**: `AilakeTable` now implements `SupportsDelete` (equality/IN pushdown, matching Trino/Flink's `deleteWhere` semantics — no row-level scan-and-delete).
  - **Spark — ALTER TABLE ADD/RENAME COLUMN**: `AilakeCatalog.alterTable` no longer unconditionally throws; calls `AilakeNative.evolveSchema` via `TableChange.AddColumn`/`RenameColumn`, same static-per-call-schema limitation Trino/Flink already document.
  - **Spark — compact**: `implicits.AilakeSession.ailakeCompact(tableUri, ...)` — a plain `SparkSession` method (Spark has no native CALL-procedure syntax outside a full catalog stored-procedure API), mirroring `ailakeWrite`'s shape.
  - **Trino — multi-column (multimodal) write**: new `AilakeNative.writeBatchMulti` wrapper + `ailake.vector-columns` catalog property (JSON `[{"column","dim","metric"?,"precision"?,"modality"?}]`); when set, `ingestColumns()` emits one `ARRAY<DOUBLE>` per entry instead of the single `ailake.vector-column`, and `AilakePageSink` calls `writeBatchMulti` instead of `writeBatch`.
  - **Flink — multi-column (multimodal) write**: new `AilakeNativeLoader.writeBatchMulti` wrapper + `'vector.columns'` DDL option (same JSON shape); `AilakeVectorTableSink`/`AilakeSinkFunction` resolve N `ARRAY<FLOAT>` columns by name instead of the single `vector.column`.
  - Tests added across all three plugins (Spark: `AilakeCatalogTest`, new `AilakeTableTest`, `AilakeSparkExtensionsTest`, `AilakeNativeTest`; Trino: `AilakeNativeTest`, `VectorScanMetadataTest`, `AilakePageSinkTest`; Flink: `AilakeNativeLoaderTest`, `AilakeVectorConnectorFactoryTest`, `AilakeVectorTableSinkTest`). Docs: `JVM_INTEGRATION.md` and `JVM_PLUGINS.md` ("Plugin parity (Fase 12)" section) updated; `CLAUDE.md` gained a Fase 12 entry.

- **`spark-plugin`/`trino-plugin`/`ailake-flink` — `ailake_scan_json` (search + full-row fetch, no JOIN needed) wired into all three (Fase 11)** — before this, SQL search in every plugin returned only `(row_id, distance, file_path)`; getting real columns (`chunk_text`, `document_title`, ...) back required a manual `JOIN` against a separately-registered Iceberg connector table pointing at the same physical location. `ailake_scan_json` (search + full-row fetch in one native call) already existed and was proven via the DuckDB extension, but had zero JVM plugin wrapper. Closed per-engine — discovered along the way that `ailake_scan_json` always returns the full row width (no column-subset filter), which meant none of the three needed a new catalog/DDL property to select columns:
  - **Spark**: `AilakeNative.scan()` JNA wrapper + `implicits.AilakeSession.ailakeSearchWithData(tableUri, queryVector, topK, vectorColumn=...)` returns a `DataFrame` with a fully dynamic schema built from the response's `schema` array (`int64`→`LongType`, `float32`→`FloatType`, `float64`→`DoubleType`, `bool`→`BooleanType`, `utf8`→`StringType`, `list_float32`→`ArrayType(FloatType)`).
  - **Trino**: new `ailake.default.search_full` table — schema is `ingestColumns()` (reusing the existing `ailake.text-columns` catalog config, no new property) `+ _distance DOUBLE`. `ScanTableHandle` reuses the existing `VectorScanSplit` as-is; `AilakeNative.scan` vs `.search` is dispatched by table handle type in `VectorScanRecordSetProvider`, not by a new split type. The vector column comes back as `VARCHAR` (JSON-encoded, e.g. `"[0.1,-0.2]"`) rather than `ARRAY<DOUBLE>` — deliberate scope cut, avoids hand-building a Trino `Block`/`BlockBuilder` for `RecordCursor.getObject` without a live Trino SPI build to verify against.
  - **Flink**: `AilakeNativeLoader.scan()` wrapper + new `AilakeScanTableSource`/`AilakeScanInputFormat`, selected via a new `'search.mode' = 'full'` DDL option on the existing search-shaped `CREATE TABLE`. Unlike Trino, Flink's DDL already declares its own columns (schema-on-read) — the only validation is that the last declared column is `_distance` (FLOAT or DOUBLE). Supports real `ARRAY<FLOAT>` columns via `GenericArrayData`, unlike Trino's JSON-string workaround.
  - Tests added across all three (`AilakeNativeTest`/`AilakeSparkExtensionsTest`, `VectorScanMetadataTest`/`VectorScanSplitManagerTest`/`VectorScanRecordSetTest`/`AilakeNativeTest` (Kotlin), `AilakeNativeLoaderTest`/`AilakeVectorConnectorFactoryTest`/`AilakeScanTableSourceTest`). Docs: `docs/guides/JVM_INTEGRATION.md` (§3B/3D/5C/6B) and `docs/specs/JVM_PLUGINS.md` ("Search + full-row fetch, no JOIN needed" section) updated with the new entry points and examples; `CLAUDE.md` Fase 11 marked done.

- **`spark-plugin`/`trino-plugin`/`ailake-flink` — `searchMultimodal()` wired into SQL/DataFrame** — audit found `AilakeNative.searchMultimodal`/`AilakeNativeLoader.searchMultimodal` (backed by `ailake_search_multimodal_json` in `libailake_jni.so`) fully implemented in all three plugins but reachable only via direct Scala/Kotlin API calls — no SQL or DataFrame surface in any of them, the same "dead capability" gap DELETE/ALTER TABLE had before Phase K. Closed per-engine:
  - **Spark**: `implicits.AilakeSession.ailakeSearchMultimodal(tableUri, queries: Seq[(col, Array[Float], weight)], topK, ...)` returns a `DataFrame(row_id: Long, rrf_score: Double, file_path: String)`, mirroring `ailakeSearch`'s existing shape.
  - **Trino**: new `ailake.default.search_multimodal` table (`row_id bigint, rrf_score double, file_path varchar`), selected via `SET SESSION ailake.multimodal_queries = '[{"col","query","weight"}, ...]'` (JSON, csv f32 query vectors) + the existing `ailake.top_k`. Required `VectorScanSplitManager.getSplits` to actually branch on the `table` parameter it previously ignored outright — new `MultimodalScanTableHandle`/`MultimodalScanSplit`/`MultimodalScanRecordSet` types alongside the existing vector-search ones.
  - **Flink**: `AilakeInputFormat.open()` gains an `ailake.multimodal.queries` job parameter (same JSON shape as Trino) on the existing search-shaped `CREATE TABLE` — the fused RRF score reuses the fixed `distance` column slot (same physical `(BIGINT, FLOAT, STRING)` row Flink's connector always emits).
  - Docs: `docs/guides/JVM_INTEGRATION.md` (§3D/5C/6B) and `docs/specs/JVM_PLUGINS.md` ("SQL/DataFrame surface" table) updated with the new entry points and examples.

- **GitHub Sponsors** — `.github/FUNDING.yml` (`github: [ThiagoLange]`) enables the native "Sponsor" button on the repo sidebar. Sponsor badge and a "Support"/"Apoie o projeto" section added to `README.md` and `README.pt-BR.md`, linking to `github.com/sponsors/ThiagoLange`
- **Sponsors placeholder section** — `README.md`/`README.pt-BR.md` gained a "Sponsors" section with a call-to-action link; to be swapped for an auto-generated sponsor list (e.g. `github-sponsors-readme-action`) once the first sponsor signs up
- **`.github/workflows/sponsors.yml`** — weekly (+ manual) job that regenerates the `<!-- sponsors -->` block in `README.md`/`README.pt-BR.md` via `JamesIves/github-sponsors-readme-action`, then commits via a throwaway branch → PR → `gh pr merge --admin --squash` straight into `main` (bypasses the PR-required branch protection the same way an admin manual merge does). Commit/PR title carries `[skip ci]` so neither the PR nor the resulting push triggers the regular CI/release workflows. Reuses the existing `ACTIONS_PAT` secret (already bypass-listed on `main`'s ruleset for `release.yml`); needs `read:user` scope added to that token if not already present
- **`ailake_write_batch_multi_json` — JNI C-ABI export for multi-column (Phase 8 multimodal) writes** — previously, the only way to populate a table with 2+ independent vector columns (e.g. text + image embeddings on the same row, searchable via `ailake_search_multimodal_json`'s RRF fusion) was `ailake-py`'s `TableWriter.write_batch_multi` via PyO3 — there was no C-ABI equivalent, so `searchMultimodal` was reachable from every JVM plugin but never self-sufficient there: a JVM-only user could call it, but could never have written the multi-vector data it searches without first dropping into Python. New export mirrors `ailake_write_batch_json`'s JSON-envelope shape (`{"ok":true,"snapshot_id":N}` / `{"ok":false,"error":"..."}`, same `ailake_free_string` ownership contract) but accepts a `vector_columns` array (`[{"col","dim","metric","precision","modality","embeddings"}, ...]`) instead of a single `vec_col`/`embeddings` pair — first entry is the primary column used for geometric pruning, matching `TableWriter::write_batch_multi`'s existing (Rust-internal) contract. Supports `deferred`, `fts_columns`/`fts_tokenizer`, `format_version`, and extra string `columns`, same as the single-vector write. 4 new Rust unit tests (null guard, empty-`vector_columns` rejection, `ids`/`embeddings` length mismatch rejection, two-column request parsing).
- **`spark-plugin` — `AilakeNative.writeBatchMulti` + `AilakeSession.ailakeWriteMulti`** — Scala/DataFrame wrappers around the new JNI export, closing the "searchMultimodal has no write path from Spark" gap found while auditing whether every Rust-implemented capability was actually reachable from the Spark plugin. New `AilakeNative.VectorColSpec(column, dim, metric="cosine", precision="f16", modality=None)` case class describes one vector column; `writeBatchMulti(tableUri, namespace, tableName, ids, vectorColumns: Seq[(VectorColSpec, Seq[Seq[Float]])], ...)` is the low-level JNI call (same double-free-safe getString→free→parse shape as the other `AilakeNative` write functions). `ailakeWriteMulti(tableUri, df, vectorColumns: Seq[VectorColSpec], idColumn="id", ...)` is the DataFrame-friendly entry point in `implicits.AilakeSession` — validates `idColumn` is `LongType`, each `VectorColSpec.column` is `ArrayType` and present in `df`, and every other column is `StringType` (same rules `AilakeWriteHandle.resolveColumns` already enforces for the single-vector path), then collects `df` to the driver and issues one native call. Unlike `ailakeWrite` (a distributed DataSourceV2 writer, one native call per Spark partition), this is intentionally driver-side and documented as such — the JNI multi-column write contract produces one AI-Lake file with N HNSW sections per call, so there's no available partitioning strategy without either a shared cross-executor HNSW build (unsupported) or a later multi-file merge across partial column sets (not implemented); suitable for batch sizes that fit in driver memory, matching the existing driver-side design of `ailakeSearch`. **Verified with a real build**: fetched Gradle 8.14.3 and built `libailake_jni.so` from source (`cargo build --release -p ailake-jni`); `AilakeWriteBatchIntegrationTest` — `writeBatchMulti and searchMultimodal roundtrip across two real vector columns` writes a real 2-column (text dim=4, image dim=2) table and confirms RRF-fused cross-modal search returns the correct top result with a doubled RRF score (both columns agreeing on rank 1), genuinely closing the gap the previous single-column-only `searchMultimodal` test could only document. New unit tests: `AilakeNativeTest` (lib-absent/empty-input guards, `VectorColSpec` defaults, JSON shape white-box) and `AilakeSparkExtensionsTest` (lib-absent, missing `VectorColSpec`s, missing id column, unknown vector column, non-string extra column validation)
- **`trino-plugin` — DELETE, ALTER TABLE ADD/RENAME COLUMN, `CALL ailake.system.compact()`, and hybrid/full-text search session properties** — full audit of `trino-plugin` (mirroring the spark-plugin audit) found `AilakeNative.kt` already had complete, correctly-implemented wrappers for `deleteWhere`, `evolveSchema`, `searchText`, and `compact` — none of them reachable from any Trino SQL surface at all (no `ConnectorMetadata.applyDelete`/`addColumn`/`renameColumn` override, no `Connector.getProcedures()`, no session properties beyond `query_vector`/`top_k`). Closed all four:
  - **`DELETE FROM ailake.default.ingest WHERE ...`** — `VectorScanMetadata.applyFilter` inspects the pushed-down `Constraint`; if it reduces to a single-column equality/IN predicate (the only shape `AilakeNative.deleteWhere`'s equality-delete-file mechanism supports — no row-level scan-and-delete exists), it's captured on a new `AilakeIngestTableHandle` and consumed via `applyDelete`/`executeDelete`. Anything else (multi-column predicates, ranges, no WHERE clause) is rejected with a clear `TrinoException`, not a silent partial delete.
  - **`ALTER TABLE ailake.default.ingest ADD COLUMN`/`RENAME COLUMN`** — wired straight to `AilakeNative.evolveSchema`, with a Trino→Iceberg type mapper covering bigint/integer/double/real/boolean/date/varchar (this connector's own minimal type surface; other types rejected with a clear error rather than mis-mapped). Genuinely persists to the table's Iceberg schema on disk — but since this connector's in-memory schema (`ailake.text-columns`) is fixed at catalog startup, the new/renamed column won't be visible to `INSERT`/`SELECT` on the *same running Trino worker* until the catalog is reconfigured and restarted; logged as a `WARN`, not silent.
  - **`CALL ailake.system.compact()`** — new `AilakeProcedures` class registers a no-arg `Procedure` (each catalog is configured for exactly one table, so nothing to parameterize) via `Connector.getProcedures()`, same idiom Iceberg's own connector uses for `CALL iceberg.system.rollback_to_snapshot(...)`.
  - **Hybrid BM25+vector RRF search and pure full-text search** — two new session properties, `SET SESSION ailake.query_text = '...'` and `SET SESSION ailake.hybrid_weight = 0.5`, reusing the existing `ailake.default.search` table/split/record-set machinery: `query_text` alone routes to `AilakeNative.searchText` (Tantivy O(log N) when the table has an FTS index), `query_text` + `query_vector` together route to `AilakeNative.search`'s existing `hybridText` RRF-fusion path.
  All four **verified end-to-end against a real `libailake_jni.so`**, not just unit-tested: `deleteViaMetadataSpiRoundtrip` drives the real `applyFilter`→`applyDelete`→`executeDelete` chain and confirms rows are actually gone; `addColumnViaMetadataSpiRoundtrip` confirms a real schema evolution; `compactProcedureRoundtrip` confirms real file merging with all rows still searchable after; `hybridSearchViaRecordSetProviderRoundtrip` confirms both new session-property routing paths return correct real results.
- **`ailake-flink` — DELETE, ALTER TABLE ADD/RENAME COLUMN, `ailake_compact` scalar function, and hybrid/full-text search job parameters** — completed the third and last leg of this session's per-plugin audit (spark-plugin, trino-plugin, now ailake-flink). Unlike trino-plugin, `AilakeNativeLoader.kt` already had every relevant JNA function declared and Kotlin-wrapped correctly (including the safe single-`finally`-free pattern — no double-free bug here either); the gap was entirely at the SQL-surface layer, same theme as trino-plugin:
  - **`DELETE FROM ailake_docs_ingest WHERE ...`** — `AilakeVectorTableSink` now implements `SupportsDeletePushDown`; `applyDeleteFilters` accepts only a single-predicate `EQUALS`/`IN` call expression on one field (matching `deleteWhere`'s own equality-only capability), rejecting anything else so an unsupported `WHERE` clause surfaces as Flink's own "DELETE not supported" error rather than a silent partial delete.
  - **`ALTER TABLE ailake_docs_ingest ADD COLUMN`/`RENAME COLUMN`** — new `AilakeCatalog.alterTable(ObjectPath, CatalogBaseTable, List<TableChange>, Boolean)` override (Flink's structured-change SPI method, more reliable than diffing before/after schemas) maps `TableChange.AddColumn`/`ModifyColumnName` to `AilakeNativeLoader.evolveSchema`, with the same Flink→Iceberg type mapper and "static per-process schema" caveat as trino-plugin's equivalent fix. The 3-arg `alterTable` override existed already but was a complete no-op passthrough — never called `evolveSchema` at all, worse than trino-plugin's starting point (an omission) since here the hook was already sitting unused.
  - **`ailake_compact` scalar function** — new `AilakeCompactFunction : ScalarFunction`, registered via `CREATE TEMPORARY FUNCTION`; Flink SQL has no `CALL`-equivalent for connectors (unlike Trino's `Procedure` SPI), so a plain scalar function is the idiomatic fit.
  - **Hybrid BM25+vector RRF and pure full-text search** — two new job parameters, `ailake.query.text` and `ailake.hybrid.weight`, read by `AilakeInputFormat.open()` alongside the existing `ailake.query.vector` (Flink SQL has no per-query `SET SESSION`, so job parameters are the existing mechanism this connector already used) — `query.text` alone routes to `AilakeNativeLoader.searchText`, both together route to `.search`'s existing `hybridText` RRF path.
  All four **verified end-to-end against a real `libailake_jni.so`**: `deleteViaSinkSpiRoundtrip` drives the real `applyDeleteFilters`→`executeDeletion` pair and confirms rows are gone; `alterTableViaCatalogRoundtrip` confirms a real schema evolution; `compactViaFunctionRoundtrip` confirms real file merging with all rows still searchable; `hybridAndTextSearchViaInputFormatRoundtrip` confirms both new job-parameter routing paths return correct real results (including a cross-language check: the underlying `AilakeNativeLoader` calls are exercised the same way `AilakeJniIntegrationTest`'s pre-existing write/search/delete/evolve tests already were).

### Fixed

- **`develop` had never received the `v0.1.1` release's version-bump commit; every other independently-versioned artifact in the repo was unified to `0.1.1` too** — the release workflow (`.github/workflows/release.yml`) only ever runs against `main`, bumping every `Cargo.toml` (Rust crates + `ailake-py`, whose PyPI version is `dynamic = ["version"]` sourced from `Cargo.toml` via maturin) and pushing a `chore: bump version to X [skip ci]` commit + tag — but that commit is never merged back into `develop`, so `develop`'s 13 `Cargo.toml` files (workspace root + `ailake-core/-catalog/-cli/-file/-fts/-index/-jni/-parquet/-py/-query/-store/-vec`, plus every internal `path`+`version` inter-crate dependency pin) had silently drifted back down to `0.1.0` — the pre-`v0.1.1` value — despite `v0.1.1` having been tagged on `main` a week earlier. Fixed by cherry-picking the release bot's version-bump commit (`17829666`) onto `develop`, a clean no-conflict apply since it only ever touches `Cargo.toml` files. Verified with `cargo check --workspace` (all 13 crates report `v0.1.1`, builds clean).
  - Went further per explicit request: unified every other independently-versioned artifact in the monorepo to `0.1.1` too — `spark-plugin`/`trino-plugin`/`ailake-flink`'s `build.gradle.kts` (`0.1.0`), `duckdb-ailake`/`ailake-cpp`'s `CMakeLists.txt` `project(... VERSION ...)` (`0.0.17`/`0.0.10`), and `airflow-providers-ailake`/`airbyte-destination-ailake`'s `pyproject.toml` (`0.0.10`/`0.0.1`) — reversing the "three independently-versioned artifacts by design" position documented in the `0.0.27` doc-fix entry below; going forward all artifacts share one version number. `ailake-go` has no hardcoded version string anywhere (Go modules version via git tags, not a manifest field) — nothing to change there.
  - Updated every doc reference to the now-stale JAR filenames this implied (`spark-plugin-0.1.0-plugin.jar` → `-0.1.1-`, same for `trino-plugin-`/`ailake-flink-`, and `JAR_VERSION=0.1.0` → `=0.1.1`) across `README.md`, `README.pt-BR.md`, `SETUP.md`, `docs/guides/JVM_INTEGRATION.md`, `docs/specs/CLOUD_DEPLOY.md`, `docs/specs/INTEGRATIONS.md`, `docs/specs/JVM_PLUGINS.md`, and the `ailake-fts` workspace-dependency example in `docs/architecture/WORKSPACE.md` — all mechanical, no version-number history in `CHANGELOG.md` itself was altered (it's a record of what was true at each past release, not a living reference).

- **`trino-plugin` — the two new Fase 12 `writeBatchMulti` tests (`AilakeNativeTest`, `AilakePageSinkTest`) assumed the native lib was absent in CI** — same bug class as `finishPassesTextColumnsAsColumnsMapToNativeWriteBatch` below: `compat-jvm-plugins` and the main `test-jvm` CI job both build `libailake_jni.so` and put it on `LD_LIBRARY_PATH`, so JNA loads it during `gradle -p trino-plugin test`. `LocalStore::new()` only strips a `file://` prefix, so the `"s3://bucket/t/"` warehouse used by `writeBatchMultiReturnsNullWhenNativeLibAbsent` fell through as a literal relative path and the write succeeded locally instead of failing like real S3 would; `finishWithVectorColumnsConfiguredReturnsEmptyWhenNativeLibAbsent` used a real writable `file:///tmp/test-table` path for the same reason. Both asserted `null`/`isEmpty()` strictly and failed whenever the write happened to succeed. Renamed and made tolerant of both outcomes (null/empty *or* a positive `snapshot_id`), matching the existing `writeBatchWithFtsColumnsDoesNotThrow` convention. Verified by building `libailake_jni.so` from source and running `gradle -p trino-plugin test` locally with the same `LD_LIBRARY_PATH`/`AILAKE_LIB_PATH` env as CI.
- **`spark-plugin` — `AilakeCatalogTest`'s `alterTable` regression test assumed the `docs` table at `file:///tmp/test-table` didn't already exist** — the `test-jvm (trino + spark plugins)` CI job runs `gradle -p trino-plugin test` then `gradle -p spark-plugin test` in the same job, sharing `/tmp` on the runner; trino-plugin's own tests write real rows to `file:///tmp/test-table/default/docs`, so by the time this Spark test ran, `evolveSchema` succeeded against the pre-existing table instead of failing, and `alterTable` returned a `Table` instead of throwing `RuntimeException`. The test only needs to prove `alterTable` makes a real `evolveSchema` call instead of the old blanket `UnsupportedOperationException`, so it doesn't need to require failure — made it tolerant of both outcomes. Verified by running `gradle -p trino-plugin test` then `gradle -p spark-plugin test` back to back locally with the same env/paths as CI, reproducing the failure on the old assertion and confirming the fix.
- **`ailake-flink` — vector search silently ignored the catalog's configured `namespace`/`vector-column`; `AilakeCatalog` never wired table identity into created tables; `ALTER TABLE` was a no-op; null id/vector went unchecked; write-tuning knobs were unreachable; the source's output schema was hardcoded** — full audit found 6 real bugs, all fixed together with the SQL-surface work above (same branch, same root-cause theme of "capability exists in Kotlin/JNA but the Flink-facing wiring around it is wrong or missing"):
  1. **`AilakeVectorTableSource.nextRecord()` always emitted a fixed `(row_id BIGINT, distance FLOAT, file_path STRING)` row regardless of the declared DDL schema** — the connector's own doc example used to show one 4-column table shape for BOTH source and sink, which would deserialize-crash on `SELECT` the moment a user followed it. `AilakeVectorConnectorFactory.createDynamicTableSource` now validates the declared schema matches the actual fixed output shape exactly, throwing a clear `ValidationException` at DDL-resolution time instead of an opaque runtime crash; the KDoc/docs now show the correct two-DDL-shape design (matching Spark/Trino's separate ingest/search tables).
  2. **`AilakeCatalog.createTable` never injected `table-name`/`namespace` into created tables** — `table-name` is a *required* connector option with no default, so any `CREATE TABLE` through this catalog failed `FactoryUtil` validation unless the user redundantly re-specified `table-name` (and `namespace`) inside `WITH(...)`, defeating the point of a catalog. Also, the catalog's own `default-namespace` configuration was never propagated to created tables at all. Both now injected from `ObjectPath`/`defaultNamespace` when not already present.
  3. **`AilakeCatalog.alterTable` (3-arg overload) was already a complete no-op passthrough** — only ever swapped Flink's in-memory `CatalogBaseTable`; `ALTER TABLE` appeared to succeed while never touching the real table. Fixed as part of the new `List<TableChange>` overload above.
  4. **`AilakeSinkFunction.invoke()` had no null-check on id/vector columns** (extra text columns did, with an empty-string fallback) — `row.getLong(idIdx)`/`row.getArray(vecIdx)` on a null field threw an opaque `NullPointerException` instead of a clear validation error naming the actual problem.
  5. **`hnsw.m`/`hnsw.ef-construction`/`pre-normalize`/`deferred` write-tuning knobs were unreachable from any DDL option** — `AilakeNativeLoader.writeBatch` already accepted all four, but nothing exposed them and `AilakeSinkFunction.flush()` always passed the defaults. New `hnsw.m`/`hnsw.ef-construction`/`pre-normalize`/`deferred` catalog options, threaded end to end.
  6. **No validation that id/vector columns had the right Flink logical types** — a mismatch (e.g. the incorrect `id STRING` shown in an earlier version of this same doc) surfaced only as an opaque `ClassCastException` deep in `RowData` extraction on the first row. `AilakeVectorTableSink.getSinkRuntimeProvider` now validates `id: BIGINT` / vector column: `ARRAY` up front with a clear message naming the column and expected type.
  Also corrected `docs/guides/JVM_INTEGRATION.md`'s Flink section (§6), which had multiple stale/wrong details: DDL option names that don't exist in the code (`table.uri`/`dim`/`metric`/`precision` — the real keys are `warehouse`+`table-name`+`vector.dim`/`vector.metric`/`vector.precision`), a wrong documented default for `metric` (doc said `cosine`, code default is `euclidean`), and two Kotlin API examples that don't type-check against the real signatures (`writeBatch`'s `ids`/`embeddings` params, and `searchMultimodal`'s `Triple` field order — was `(weight, col, query)`, is actually `(col, query, weight)`).
  **Verified with a real build**: fetched Gradle 8.14.3, built `libailake_jni.so` from source. New regression tests for all 6 bugs (`AilakeCatalogTest`, `AilakeVectorTableSinkTest`, `AilakeVectorConnectorFactoryTest`) plus the SQL-surface tests above. 67 tests total, 0 failures, both with and without the native lib present.

- **`trino-plugin` — vector search silently ignored the catalog's configured `namespace`, `table-name`, and `vector-column`** — `VectorScanTableHandle` (the search-table handle, distinct from the write-path's `AilakeIngestTableHandle`) only ever carried `tableUri`/`vectorColumn`/`dim`; `VectorScanMetadata.getTableHandle` dropped its own `namespace`/`tableName` fields when constructing it, and `VectorScanRecordSetProvider.getRecordSet` called `AilakeNative.search(tableUri, queryBytes, topK)` with no namespace/table/vector-column arguments at all — falling back to `AilakeNative.search`'s hardcoded `namespace="default"` and URI-derived table name. Worse, `search()` never sent a `vec_col` field in its native request payload in the first place (confirmed by reading the full function body — `writeBatch()` sends `vec_col`, `search()` didn't), always defaulting to the native side's own `"embedding"` fallback. A catalog configured with `ailake.namespace`, a `vector-column` other than `embedding`, or a `table-uri` whose last path segment doesn't match `table-name` would write correctly but silently search the wrong (usually empty) table/column, with zero test coverage catching it. `VectorScanTableHandle`/`VectorScanSplit` now carry `namespace`/`tableName`/`vectorColumn` end to end, and `AilakeNative.search` gained a `vectorColumn` parameter that's now always sent as `vec_col`. Regression tests: `VectorScanMetadataTest` — `getTableHandleCarriesNamespaceAndTableName`; `VectorScanSplitManagerTest` — `splitCarriesNamespaceTableNameAndVectorColumnFromHandle`
- **`trino-plugin` — `AilakePageSink.appendPage` had no null-check on the vector column** — the `id` column had an auto-generated-id fallback and text columns had an empty-string fallback for `NULL`, but the vector column (`vecBlock`) was passed straight into `extractVector` with no `isNull` check — a `NULL` embedding either threw an obscure exception from `Block.getObject`/`positionCount` or silently produced a wrong-length vector that would corrupt `AilakeNative.writeBatch`'s `ids`/`embeddings` batch for every row in the same `INSERT`, not just the offending one. `AilakePageSink.appendPage` now fails fast with a clear message naming the vector column on any `NULL` position; `VectorScanMetadata.ingestColumns()` also declares the `embedding` column `NOT NULL` (via `ColumnMetadata.builder()`) so Trino itself should reject the `INSERT` before a page ever reaches the sink — the sink-level check is defense in depth. Regression test: `AilakePageSinkTest` — `appendPageThrowsClearErrorOnNullEmbedding`
- **`trino-plugin` — `hnsw_m`/`hnsw_ef_construction`/`pre_normalize`/`deferred`/FTS-column write-tuning knobs were unreachable from any catalog property** — `AilakeNative.writeBatch` already accepted all six parameters, but `AilakePageSink.finish()`'s call to it always omitted them (so they silently took their defaults), and there was no `ailake.*` catalog property to configure any of them — including `ailake.text-columns`, whose values were only ever wired to the generic `columns` map (real data, correctly stored) but never to `fts_columns`, so a Tantivy FTS index was never built for them even though that's presumably why a user would declare them. New catalog properties `ailake.hnsw-m`, `ailake.hnsw-ef-construction`, `ailake.pre-normalize`, `ailake.deferred`, `ailake.fts-columns` (separate list from `ailake.text-columns`, analogous to Flink's `fts.columns`), `ailake.fts-tokenizer` — threaded through `VectorScanConnectorFactory` → `VectorScanConnector` → `VectorScanMetadata` → `AilakeIngestTableHandle` → `AilakePageSink.finish()`. Regression tests: `AilakePageSinkTest` — `handleCarriesWriteTuningKnobsThroughToDefaults`, `handleCarriesConfiguredWriteTuningKnobs`
- **`spark-plugin` — double-free of the JNA-returned string pointer on JSON parse failure in `writeBatch`/`deleteWhere`/`evolveSchema`/`compact`** — all four `AilakeNative` functions freed the native pointer (`ailake_free_string(ptr)`) immediately after reading it, then continued parsing the resulting JSON string (`mapper.readTree(json)`, `root.path(...)`) inside the *same* try block; if that parsing threw (malformed/truncated JSON from the native side), the `catch` block called `ailake_free_string(ptr)` a second time on an already-freed pointer — undefined behavior across the JNI boundary, able to crash the JVM outright rather than degrade gracefully. `search()` already had the correct shape (read the string, free unconditionally, *then* parse in a separate try/catch); the other four now match it: `getString`/free happens first and unconditionally, parsing failures after that point no longer touch the pointer again. No dedicated regression test for the malformed-JSON edge itself (reproducing it requires the native library to actually return malformed JSON, which doesn't happen in practice), but the refactored success path for all four functions is now exercised end-to-end against a real compiled `libailake_jni.so`: `writeBatch`/`deleteWhere`/`evolveSchema` already had real-library integration tests, and this PR adds one for `compact` (`AilakeWriteBatchIntegrationTest` — `compact merges small files`, writes 5 small batches then asserts `filesCompacted >= 1` and all 10 rows remain searchable post-compact)
- **`spark-plugin` — `compact` and `searchMultimodal` had zero coverage against a real native library** — every other `AilakeNative` function (`writeBatch`, `search`, `searchText`, `deleteWhere`, `evolveSchema`) had a real-library integration test; these two only had lib-absent unit tests, so nothing had ever verified their real JNI request/response wiring actually round-trips correctly. Added `compact merges small files` (writes 5 small batches, compacts with `minFiles=2`, asserts files were actually merged and all rows remain searchable) and `searchMultimodal returns real results against a single real vector column` (writes a real table, calls `searchMultimodal` with one query column, asserts the RRF-fused result is correct) to `AilakeWriteBatchIntegrationTest`. Note: `searchMultimodal`'s cross-*modal* fusion across two or more distinct vector columns on the same table remains untestable from Spark (or Trino/Flink) alone — `ailake_write_batch_json`'s JNI request only accepts a single `vec_col`; multi-vector-column write (`write_multi`) exists only in the Python SDK via PyO3, with no equivalent in the `ailake-jni` C-ABI. `searchMultimodal` is reachable from Spark but can only be exercised end-to-end against a table a Python job populated first
- **Cross-language fixture regression check** — `AilakeNativeIntegrationTest` (Spark's JNA-bridge smoke test, reading a fixture written by `tests/fixtures/write_jni_fixture.py` via raw `ctypes`) was re-verified against a freshly built `libailake_jni.so`: data written outside the JVM (pure Python/ctypes, bypassing both the Rust SDK's Python bindings and any JVM plugin) round-trips correctly through `AilakeNative.search`, confirming the JSON request/response envelope is stable across languages, not just internally consistent within Spark's own write path
- **`spark-plugin` — `AilakeCatalog.loadTable` (bare `INSERT INTO ailake.ns.table VALUES (...)`, no known DataFrame schema) threw for any catalog configured with a non-default `vector-column` name** — `loadTable` built its fallback schema from `AilakeTable.WRITE_SCHEMA`, which hardcoded the vector field's name to the literal `"embedding"`; `AilakeWriteHandle.resolveColumns`' `schema.fieldIndex(vectorColumn)` lookup then failed with `IllegalArgumentException` whenever `spark.sql.catalog.ailake.vector-column` was set to anything else — even though this is a documented, supported catalog option, and even though `AilakeCatalogTest` asserts `tableExists` (backed by `loadTable`) never throws. New `AilakeTable.defaultSchema(vectorColumn)` builds the 2-column fallback schema using the configured name instead of a fixed literal; `WRITE_SCHEMA` is now just `defaultSchema("embedding")`. Regression test: `AilakeCatalogTest` — `loadTable with custom vector-column name does not throw and uses that name in the schema`
- **`spark-plugin` — `AilakeWriteHandle.resolveColumns` validated extra (text) column types but not `id`/vector column types** — a `CREATE TABLE` with e.g. `id INT` or `embedding ARRAY<FLOAT>` (looser than the historical `id BIGINT, embedding ARRAY<DOUBLE>`) passed schema resolution silently, since only non-id/non-vector columns were type-checked, and only failed later with an opaque `ClassCastException` inside `AilakeDataWriter.write`'s unchecked `row.getLong`/`row.getArray(...).toDoubleArray()`. `resolveColumns` now validates `id` is `LongType` and the vector column is `ArrayType(DoubleType)` up front, raising the same kind of clear `IllegalArgumentException` (naming the column and expected type) the text-column check already gave. Regression tests: `AilakeWriteHandle.resolveColumns rejects non-Long id column`, `rejects non-array<double> vector column`, `accepts nullable array<double> vector column`
- **`spark-plugin` — `ailakeSearch` had no `namespace`/`tableName` parameters, unlike `ailakeWrite`** — writing to a non-default namespace (`ailakeWrite(..., namespace = "prod")` or a SQL-catalog table like `ailake.prod.docs`) was then unfindable via `spark.ailakeSearch(...)`, which always searched `AilakeNative.search`'s hardcoded `namespace = "default"` — a silent, empty-result failure mode (only a `WARN` log), not an error. `ailakeSearch` now accepts `namespace`/`tableName` parameters (same defaults and resolution rule as `ailakeWrite`) and threads them through to `AilakeNative.search`. Regression test: `AilakeSparkExtensionsTest` — `ailakeSearch accepts namespace and tableName parameters`
- **`spark-plugin` — `ailakeWrite`'s `idColumn` option was accepted but never read anywhere** — documented as "id column name in the DataFrame" and passed via `.option("idColumn", idColumn)`, but `AilakeDataSource.buildSchema` hardcoded the id field name to `"id"` and `AilakeWriteHandle.resolveColumns` hardcoded `schema.fieldIndex("id")` — a caller with an id column actually named e.g. `doc_id` got a confusing `AnalysisException: cannot resolve 'id'` that had nothing to do with their real mistake (there wasn't one). `resolveColumns` now takes an `idColumn` parameter (default `"id"`, backward-compatible), and `AilakeDataSource` reads the `idColumn`/`id-column` option and threads it through to both `buildSchema` and `resolveColumns`. Regression tests: `AilakeWriteHandle.resolveColumns resolves a custom idColumn name`, `AilakeDataSource.buildSchema respects idColumn option`
- **`spark-plugin` — misleading doc comment on `VectorSearchPlan` claiming an `ailake_vector_search(...)` SQL syntax exists** — no parser/function is registered anywhere in the module (`AilakeSparkExtensions.apply` only injects the planner strategy), and the plan is never actually executed through Spark's planner in production — the only real caller, `ailakeSearch`, builds it solely to borrow its output `schema` and calls `AilakeNative.search` directly. `VectorScanStrategy`/`VectorScanExec` remain reachable only from tests that manually drive `spark.sessionState.executePlan(...)`. Doc comment corrected to describe the actual (unreachable-from-SQL) code path instead of a feature that was never wired up; left the strategy/exec machinery in place as-is (no behavior change, doc-only fix — wiring up real SQL parsing is a larger feature, not a bug fix)
- **`trino-plugin` — the `ailake.default.ingest` table's schema was hardcoded to exactly `(id, embedding)`, with no way to write extra text/metadata columns at all** — worse than the equivalent Spark gap (fixed separately): Trino doesn't support `CREATE TABLE`/DDL for this connector (`AilakePageSinkProvider` throws `UnsupportedOperationException` on CTAS), so the ingest schema is entirely code-defined and was a fixed 2-column `val` (`VectorScanMetadata.INGEST_COLUMNS`/`INGEST_COLUMN_HANDLES`) — there was no code path, not even a hypothetical one, for a user to declare a 3rd column. `AilakePageSink.appendPage` correspondingly only ever read `page.getBlock(0)`/`getBlock(1)` and called `AilakeNative.writeBatch(...)` without ever setting the `columns` parameter (silently defaulting to `emptyMap()`), even though the native bridge already supports it — proven by the plugin's own integration test (`AilakeWriteBatchIntegrationTest.kt:210`) calling `AilakeNative.writeBatch` directly with a real `columns` map, bypassing the SQL write path entirely. Extra columns are now declared catalog-wide via `ailake.text-columns` (comma-separated, analogous to Flink's `fts.columns`) — `VectorScanMetadata.ingestColumns()` builds `(id, embedding, ...textColumns VARCHAR)` dynamically instead of returning the old fixed `val`s, `AilakeIngestTableHandle` carries the resolved `textColumns` list through to `AilakePageSink`, which now accumulates each extra VARCHAR channel per row and passes `columns = textValues` into `writeBatch`. **Verified with a real build**: no Gradle wrapper or system Gradle was present, so `gradle-8.14.3-bin.zip` was fetched directly via `curl` (same workaround as the Spark/Flink/DuckDB fixes) and used to compile + run the full existing `trino-plugin` test suite (all pre-existing tests still pass) plus new regression tests: `AilakeIngestMetadataTest` (schema/column-handle wiring for `textColumns`, ordinal correctness, empty-by-default) and `AilakePageSinkTest` (`appendPage` accumulating real per-row VARCHAR values from a hand-built Trino `Page`/`Block`, verified via reflection against the private `textValues` buffer, plus the no-textColumns-configured path still reading only id+embedding)
- **`trino-plugin` — `AilakePageSinkTest.finishPassesTextColumnsAsColumnsMapToNativeWriteBatch` assumed `finish()` always returns empty fragments** — true locally (no `libailake_jni.so`), false in CI's `test-jvm` job (sets `AILAKE_LIB_PATH` to a real compiled lib), where `finish()` performs a real write against the test's fake `tableUri` and returns a non-empty fragment list, failing the hardcoded `isEmpty` assertion. Same bug class as the `spark-plugin` columns-map test fix. Drops the `finish()` call and inspects the sink's private `textValues` buffer via reflection right after `appendPage()` instead — deterministic regardless of native lib presence; the native `writeBatch` call itself is already covered by this file's existing native-lib-gated integration tests
- **`ailake-flink` — any DDL-declared column not also listed in the `fts.columns` connector option was silently dropped from the write** — narrower version of the same bug class fixed in `spark-plugin`/`trino-plugin`. `AilakeVectorTableSink`'s schema is fully user-defined via `CREATE TABLE` DDL (`AilakeVectorConnectorFactory.createDynamicTableSink` passes `context.catalogTable.resolvedSchema` straight through), and the `fts.columns`-designated path was already correctly wired end-to-end (verified: real per-row values flow from `RowData` through `AilakeSinkFunction.invoke()`'s buffers into `columns=` in the native call, which the Rust JNI side turns into real persisted `Utf8` Parquet columns). But `columns` is a general persisted-metadata mechanism, not an FTS-only one — a column like `source STRING` declared in DDL but not listed in `'fts.columns'` was real per-row data Flink hands to `invoke()`'s `RowData` every time, yet the old `ftsColumnIndices` map never included it, so it was read then discarded on every row. Extracted `AilakeVectorTableSink.computeExtraColumnIndices()` (now `internal`, independently unit-tested) to include every declared **STRING** column except id/vector — not just the `fts.columns` subset — and renamed the field it feeds (`AilakeSinkFunction.extraColumnIndices`, was `ftsColumnIndices`); `fts.columns` still separately controls which of those get a Tantivy FTS index. Non-string extra columns (e.g. a `_distance FLOAT` column shared with the source side of the same table, previously "ignored on write" by design) are still correctly skipped — `columns=` is `Map<String, List<String>>` on the native side, there's nowhere to put a non-string value. Also corrected the stale doc comment on `AilakeVectorTableSink` ("Any number of additional columns (currently ignored — future: stored in Parquet)"), which predated the `fts.columns` wiring and overstated the gap. **Verified with a real build**: no Gradle wrapper or system Gradle was present, so `gradle-8.14.3-bin.zip` was fetched directly via `curl` (same workaround as the Spark/Trino/DuckDB fixes) and used to compile + run the existing `ailake-flink` test suite (all pre-existing tests still pass) plus a new `AilakeVectorTableSinkTest`: `computeExtraColumnIndices` unit tests (includes every string column regardless of `fts.columns`, skips non-string columns, empty when only id+embedding declared) and `AilakeSinkFunction.invoke()` tests against real `GenericRowData`/`StringData` rows, verifying actual per-row values land in the sink's `textBuffers` via reflection (including the null-value-as-empty-string case)
- **`spark-plugin` — the native write path silently dropped every DataFrame column except `id`/`embedding`** — `AilakeDataSource`/`AilakeTable`/`AilakeWriteBuilder` hardcoded the write schema to `(id, embedding)`, even though `AilakeNative.writeBatch` already accepts a `columns: Map[String, Seq[String]]` parameter (the Flink connector, `AilakeVectorTableSink`, already wires this through — Spark never did). This made `df.write.format("io.ailake.spark.AilakeDataSource")` unusable for RAG-shaped writes: chunk text/metadata had no way to travel alongside the vectors through the native path at all. `TableProvider.inferSchema` only ever receives write options, never the caller's DataFrame, and Spark validates the write against `inferSchema()`'s output before `getTable()` sees real data — so extra columns must be declared explicitly via `.option("textColumns", "text,source,page")` rather than auto-detected from the DataFrame; declared columns must be `StringType` (`AilakeWriteHandle.resolveColumns` raises a clear `IllegalArgumentException` otherwise, naming the offending column). `AilakeCatalog.createTable` (SQL `CREATE TABLE`) gets the same fix — it already received a real resolved schema from Spark and was discarding it, delegating to `loadTable` instead. **Verified with a real build**: no Gradle wrapper or system Gradle was present, so `gradle-8.14.3-bin.zip` was fetched directly via `curl` (same workaround as the Flink/DuckDB fixes) and used to compile + run the existing `spark-plugin` test suite (all pre-existing tests still pass) plus four new regression tests in `AilakeNativeTest.scala` covering the `textColumns` option, the historical id+embedding-only default, the `IllegalArgumentException` on a non-string extra column, and `AilakeDataWriter` accumulating per-column buffers correctly. Beyond the test suite: built the `shadowJar`, loaded it into a real local Spark 3.5.6 session with `libailake_jni.so` on `java.library.path`, wrote a DataFrame with `id`+`embedding`+`text`+`source`+`page` through the actual native `AilakeDataSource` path, and confirmed the Parquet output round-trips every column correctly
- **Docs — stale `0.0.27` version references across `README.md`, `README.pt-BR.md`, `ailake-py/README.md`, `docs/guides/JVM_INTEGRATION.md`, `docs/specs/JVM_PLUGINS.md`, `docs/specs/CLOUD_DEPLOY.md`** — the repo has three independently-versioned artifacts (Rust crates/PyPI `ailake` at `0.1.1`, JVM plugin JARs built by gradle at `0.1.0`, `apache-airflow-providers-ailake` at `0.0.10`), but install snippets used a single `VERSION` shell var to template both the GitHub release tag and the JAR filename — broken for any value once the two diverged, since the tag (`v0.1.1`) and the actual JAR asset name (`spark-plugin-0.1.0-plugin.jar`) no longer match. Split into `TAG` (release tag) and `JAR_VERSION` (gradle plugin version) in every JVM install snippet; bumped Cargo/PyPI dependency examples and `pip` version pins to `0.1.1`

## [0.1.1] — 2026-07-02

### Added

- **Foreign-write detection and repair prioritization** (ADR-018, `docs/contributing/DECISIONS.md`) — a generic Iceberg engine (Spark/Trino `OPTIMIZE`/`rewrite_data_files`, DuckDB) can legally rewrite an AI-Lake data file with no knowledge of AI-Lake, producing valid Parquet with no AILK footer and no `centroid`/`radius` in its manifest entry. This degrades affected files to an exact O(N) flat scan at query time (already the existing fallback in `scanner.rs`) rather than corrupting data, but was previously silent. `CompactionPlanner::plan()` now detects any file with no `centroid_b64` (never written by the AI-Lake SDK) and prioritizes it for reindex, bypassing `min_files_to_compact`/size thresholds — a single foreign file triggers repair on its own. `scanner.rs::search` now distinguishes expected deferred-indexing fallback (`debug!`) from unexpected foreign-write fallback (`warn!`, with an aggregate summary per search call). `ailake info` reports foreign-file paths (`foreign_files`/`foreign_file_paths` in `--format json`) for proactive drift detection without needing a slow query to notice
- `AilakeFileReader::verify_integrity()` (`parquet_count == hnsw_node_count == header.record_count`) now runs after every compaction merge (`compact()`/`compact_incremental()`) and after every deferred index build (`writer.rs::build_and_patch_index` — shared by plain deferred inserts and `compact_deferred()`'s background job), before the result is committed to the catalog — previously only exercised by tests, so a mismatched merge could reach the manifest undetected
- `DataFileEntry::is_foreign()` (`ailake-catalog`) — single shared definition of "never written by the AI-Lake SDK" (no `centroid_b64`), used by `CompactionPlanner::plan()`, `scanner.rs::search`, and `ailake info` so the three can't drift on what counts as foreign

### Fixed

- **`ailake-file` — corrupted/foreign AI-Lake files could panic the reader instead of returning `NotAnAilakeFile`** — `read_header_at_offset`, `get_centroid`, `load_index_for_column`, and `load_any_index_for_column` all added untrusted header offset/length fields (parsed straight from file bytes with no bound checks) using plain `usize` addition. A crafted or corrupted file with e.g. `hnsw_offset` near `u64::MAX` could overflow the addition — in a release build the wrapped result could slip past the `> self.bytes.len()` bounds check and panic later on a backwards slice range, reachable from every public read entry point. Now uses `checked_add`, erroring cleanly instead. Regression test: `ailake-file/src/reader.rs::corrupted_hnsw_offset_errors_instead_of_panicking`
- **`ailake-query` — compaction's `Replace` snapshot was never chained to its parent** — `CompactionExecutor::run()`/`run_deferred()` hardcoded `parent_snapshot_id: None` even though a current snapshot always exists (compaction only runs on an already-populated table), breaking Iceberg snapshot lineage (`expire_snapshots`/`rollback_to_snapshot`) for any table that's ever been compacted. Every sibling caller (`migration.rs`, `memory_decay.rs`, `delete.rs`) already set this correctly. Now fetched fresh right before commit, same freshness rationale as the existing file-list re-list. Regression assertion added to `run_preserves_untouched_files_outside_compaction_pass` (reads the committed `metadata.json` directly, since no public `CatalogProvider` method exposes snapshot lineage)
- **`ailake-store` — `ObjectStoreBackend::resolve()` didn't strip absolute-URI scheme prefixes** — unlike `LocalStore::full_path` (which strips `file://` so `PathBuf::join`'s absolute-path override works), an absolute path like `s3://bucket/warehouse/ns/table/data/part.parquet` (the shape `HadoopCatalog` stores in `DataFileEntry.path` when the warehouse root itself is absolute) was concatenated onto the configured `prefix` verbatim, producing a garbage double-prefixed key on every S3/GCS/Azure read. Now strips `scheme://bucket/` and uses the remaining key directly when the input path is already absolute. Regression tests in `ailake-store/src/object_store_backend.rs`
- **`ailake-cli` — `compact` had no `--deferred`/`--max-files-per-pass` flags and fabricated its result** — the CLI's `Compact` command manually re-implemented planning/committing instead of using `CompactionExecutor::run()`/`run_deferred()` (already fixed above), so it couldn't expose deferred indexing or per-pass file limits at all — `ailake-go`'s `SearchHybrid`-adjacent compact callers and `ailake-py`'s `compact()` Python wrapper both silently dropped `deferred`/`max_files_per_pass` because the flags never existed. `ailake-py`'s wrapper also always returned `{"ok": True, "files_compacted": 1}` on any zero-exit-code run, including a real no-op ("nothing to compact"). `Compact` now delegates to `CompactionExecutor::run()`/`run_deferred()` directly (matching `ailake_compact_json`'s JNI behavior and reusing its now-correct `parent_snapshot_id`), gained `--deferred`, `--max-files-per-pass`, and `--format json` (emitting `{"ok":true,"files_compacted":0|1,"output_path":...}`, matching JNI's `files_compacted` semantics exactly), and the Python wrapper now passes both flags through and parses the real JSON response instead of fabricating one
- **`ailake-cli` — `search` had no hybrid BM25+vector flags, breaking every `ailake-go` `SearchHybrid` call** — `Search`'s vector-search branch hardcoded `hybrid: None` in `SearchConfig`, so `ailake-go`'s `SearchHybrid` (which already sent `--hybrid-text`/`--text-column`/`--bm25-weight`, expecting the CLI to support them) failed every call with a clap "unrecognized argument" error — the Go binding's code was correct, the CLI just never grew the flags it assumed existed. Added `--hybrid-text`, `--text-column` (default `"chunk_text"`), and `--bm25-weight` (default `0.5`), wired into `HybridConfig`. No Go-side change needed. Regression test: `tests/tests/cli_hybrid_search.rs` (drives the real compiled CLI binary end-to-end)
- **`duckdb-ailake` — every write/search/delete/evolve function was pinned to `default.table`/`default.<table_path-derived-name>` regardless of caller intent** — `ailake_write_batch` documented `namespace`/`table_name` as overridable in its header comment, but no registered arity included them and both were hardcoded literals in `AilakeWriteExecFull`; `ailake_delete_where` and `ailake_evolve_schema` had no override at all; `ailake_search`/`ailake_search_text`/`ailake_scan` already supported a `table_name` named parameter (added in an earlier pass) but not `namespace`; `ailake_search_multimodal` had neither. Every one of these hardcoded `"namespace":"default"` directly into the native JSON request in `AilakeLib`'s methods (`ailake_extension.cpp`), so passing a different value anywhere had no effect regardless of arity. Added `ns` (default `"default"`) as a real parameter threaded through `AilakeLib::search/search_text/search_multimodal/scan/delete_where/evolve_schema`; exposed as a `namespace` named parameter on the table functions (`ailake_search`, `ailake_search_text`, `ailake_search_multimodal`, `ailake_scan`) and as new trailing positional arities on the scalar functions (`ailake_write_batch` arity 17+18 for `namespace`+`table_name`; `ailake_delete_where` and `ailake_evolve_schema` arity 5 for both). `ailake_search_multimodal` also gained the `table_name` named parameter it was missing entirely. **Verified with a real build**: this workspace has no git access to fetch DuckDB's source directly (network hangs on the git protocol specifically; HTTPS works), so the exact `v1.5.3` source tarball and the `nlohmann/json` release tarball referenced by the extension's `CMakeLists.txt` were fetched via `curl` instead and pointed at via `FETCHCONTENT_SOURCE_DIR_DUCKDB`/`FETCHCONTENT_SOURCE_DIR_NLOHMANN_JSON`, letting `cmake --build` compile and link the real extension from scratch. Loaded into the `duckdb` Python package (`RTLD_GLOBAL` + `allow_extensions_metadata_mismatch`, the same workaround already used by this project's own `test/*.py` harness) and ran the full existing `duckdb-ailake/test/*.py` suite (all pre-existing tests still pass — no regression) plus two new regression tests: `test_write.py::test_write_with_namespace_and_table_name` (writes to `<dir>/custom_ns/my_table` via the new arity-18 call and confirms the Parquet file lands there, not under the old hardcoded `default/table`) and `test_search.py::test_search_namespace_named_param_isolation` (writes under `custom_ns`, confirms `ailake_search(..., namespace := 'custom_ns', table_name := 'my_table')` finds the rows and a plain default-namespace search finds none — proving real isolation, not just an accepted-but-ignored parameter)
- **`ailake-flink` — a missing native library crashed the whole Flink task instead of returning empty results** — `AilakeNativeLoader.lib` is `by lazy { ... }.getOrThrow()`, and every method reads it eagerly with no guard, unlike Spark (`Option[Lib]`) and Trino (`Lib?`), which both resolve to a nullable handle and degrade to empty results — the same documented "graceful degradation" contract this codebase enforces elsewhere. `AilakeInputFormat.open()` now catches native-load failures (`UnsatisfiedLinkError` and friends surface as JVM `Error`s, not `Exception`s, so the catch is intentionally broad) and falls back to an empty result iterator with a warning log, instead of letting the exception fail the task. The write path (`AilakeVectorTableSink`) is intentionally left as-is: silently dropping a write batch on a missing native lib would be data loss, not a safe degradation, so it should keep failing loudly. **Verified with a real build**: no Gradle wrapper or system Gradle was present, so the `gradle-8.7-bin.zip` distribution was fetched directly via `curl` (same workaround as the DuckDB extension fix) and used to run `gradle compileKotlin`/`gradle test` against the real Flink 1.18.1 + Kotlin 1.9.23 dependencies — compiles clean (only pre-existing deprecation warnings, none in the changed file). Added `AilakeVectorTableSourceTest` with two new regression tests exercising `open()` with a mocked `RuntimeContext` and no native lib on the classpath (guaranteed absent in this env): `openDoesNotThrowWhenNativeLibMissing` and `openWithoutNativeLibLeavesResultSetEmpty`, both passing (0 failures across all 32 tests in the module, no regressions in the 3 pre-existing test classes)
- **`ailake-cpp` — `search_text()` misread `pclose()`'s exit status, reporting bogus error codes** — `pclose()` returns a POSIX wait-status, not a plain exit code (real code `N` shows up as `N << 8`, e.g. exit 1 reported as 256) — it must go through `WIFEXITED`/`WEXITSTATUS` first. The sibling helper `write.hpp::detail::run_cmd` already does this correctly; `ailake.hpp`'s independent `popen`/`pclose` block in `search_text()` never received the same fix. Regression test: `ailake-cpp/tests/test_fts.cpp::test_search_text_reports_real_exit_code_not_raw_wait_status` (points `AILAKE_BIN` at a throwaway script that always exits 1, asserts the thrown message reports code 1, not 256) — verified via a real local CMake+ctest build (this extension, unlike `duckdb-ailake`, doesn't require fetching an external source tree)
